The author of this book completed it for you, sons. This book is a part of the science of medicine in its entirety and completion, with its clarity and distinctness. I have attained the highest level in it with respect to its explanation. I saw fit to complete it for you through this discourse which is an operation by hand.
Because the operation by hand is highly valued in our country and in our time, completely unknown until it was almost taught and its effect disappeared. And the only remaining from it were some simple diagrams in the early books which had been drawn by hand, containing errors and inaccuracies until their meanings became obscure and their benefits were lost.
I saw fit to revive it and to compile in this discourse according to the method of explanation, clarity and conciseness, and to bring forth images of surgical instruments with all their parts because it is an increase in clarification and a source for what is needed.
The reason that there is no skilled craftsman by hand in our time today is that the craft of medicine is long and its owner should be accustomed before that in the science of anatomy which Galen described. Until he is familiar with the benefits, healthiness and temperaments of the organs, their connections and separations, the knowledge of the bones, nerves, muscles, their number and exits, the arteries, veins and saphenous vessels and the places of their exits.
Therefore Ipucria said that the physicians by name are many and in fact few, especially in the craft of hand, and we have mentioned a part of this in the introduction to this book.
Because he who is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned from anatomy, has fallen into error and killed people with it, as I have seen many who have claimed knowledge in this science without knowledge or understanding.
And I have seen an ignorant doctor who cut on a pig-like growth in the neck of a woman, and he severed some of the ligaments of the neck, so that the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead before him.
I saw another physician operate on a man who had been stabbed in the groin and had a large stone. The stone was removed with a piece of the bladder wall. The man died after about three days, and I was called to remove it, and having seen the size of the stone and the nature of the wound, I estimated that.
And I saw another physician who was traveling with some horsemen from our land as a surgeon.
So I spoke to a black boy who had a fracture of the leg near the knee with an injury. The physician hurried in ignorance and bound the fracture tightly on top of the wound with strips of cloth and leather, not leaving the wound any room to breathe.
Then he released him and left him for a few days, ordering him not to untie the bandage until his leg and foot had swollen. And I watched as I was supervising his destruction.
So I was called to him, and I hurried to untie the bandage. He recovered his comfort and escaped from his pain, but the corruption had taken hold in the member, and I could not restore it.
And so the corruption continued to spread in the member until he died.
And I saw another physician who had cauterized a cancerous tumor, and it ulcerated after a few days until the patient's body was swollen. This is because if the cancer is pure black, then iron should not be applied to it at all.
Unless it be in an organ that can possibly be excised entirely.
And so, my sons, you should know that the work of the hand is divided into two parts: a work in which safety accompanies it and a work in which trouble results from it in most cases.
And I have warned you wherever this book's work comes from, which involves danger and fear, that you should beware of it and reject it.
Be cautious, for the ignorant may find their way to incision and cutting. Take precautions with yourselves, be resolute and secure, and with your patients, be gentle and stable.
And employ the better way leading to safety and the praised success, and be persistent in treating the difficult and hard-to-heal diseases.
And protect yourselves from what you fear may lead to doubt in your religion and worldly affairs, for it is better for your dignity and will elevate you in this world and the next.
For Galen said in some of his advice, Do not treat a bad disease so that you become known as bad physicians.
And this book is divided into three parts.

With caustics by fire and the sharp drug, promptly arranged in order from ancient times to the present day, and pictures of the equipment and cauterizing trays and all that is needed with the hand for work.

The First Part.
Concerning Cauterization.
And before mentioning the manner of using it, it is necessary to mention its benefits and harms, and in which temperament it should be used.
And I say that the discussion of how cauterization is beneficial and harmful is a long speech, precise knowledge, and a secret known only to a few wise people.
And they disagreed about it, and I have briefly summarized what little of their words was necessary in order not to lengthen it too much.
I say that the kawak (a type of poultice) is beneficial in general for all bad temperaments, whether accompanied by matter or not. Except two temperaments: hot without matter and cold without matter.
As for the cold temperament with matter, they differed in their opinion. Some said that the kawak is beneficial in it, while others disagreed, saying that the kawak does not cure a disease that results from heat and cold, because the nature of fire is heat and cold.
And it is unlikely that a person suffering from a hot and cold disease would be cured by a hot and cold remedy. And he who disagreed said that the kawak with fire may benefit someone suffering from a hot and cold disease in the human body. Because as soon as you add to the body of man and his humidity the temperament of fire, the body of man becomes cold.
And I say, because experience has revealed this to me on numerous occasions. Unless one who has accepted and learned in the art of kawak has contemplated it, however. And stood firm on the differences in temperaments of people and the condition of diseases themselves, their causes and symptoms, and the length of time.
And as for the other temperaments, do not be afraid of them, especially cold and damp diseases. All physicians have agreed on their treatment with kawak and have not differed in its benefit.
Know, my son, that the treatment with kawak is fire and its superiority over the medicine of burning is that fire is a single essence which does not exceed the action of the part it cauterizes except for a slight harm to an adjacent connected part.
And the kawak with burning medicine may exceed its action to beyond what it touches and may create a disease in the part that makes its treatment difficult or even fatal, whereas fire, because of its noble essence and high dignity, does not do this except if it is excessive.
And it has become clear to us through experience the length of service and care in craftsmanship and standing on the facts of the matter.
And for this reason I have dispensed with lengthy speech, but had it not been unfitting for a book like this, I would have told you in secret a more obscure and subtle manner how to do it in the bodies and deny the diseases by philosophical words and proofs that pound against your understanding.
Know, my sons, that they have differed about the time in which surgery should be performed and have considered the best time to be during spring.
And I say that surgery can be performed at any time for the harm caused by time is taken into consideration and benefits are brought about by surgery. And especially when the surgery is from necessary and strong pains that cannot be delayed because what is feared from it is a gangrene which is greater than the damage that has come from time.
And do not think, my sons, that the common people and simple doctors imagine that surgery which cures a disease will never return again and makes it easy.
And you have not thought, my sons, that surgery is only a medicine which changes the temperament and dries up the moisture which are the cause of the occurrence of pains.
But as for surgery, it excels over medicine in its quick success and strong action and sharp authority.
And it is possible for the disease to return some time from then on depending on the temperament of the patient and his ability and strength and what has been accumulated in him of bad humors and his negligence in acquiring them from food and so on.
O Allah, unless the disease in which surgery is used be a light disease and in an organ with little bad humors and moisture. Similar to the removal of a wisdom tooth from pain and similar cases, it may not return again; that is the least.
And as for the saying of the common people, also that the tooth is the end of treatment, it is a true statement not to what they go; because they assume that there is no remedy that benefits by medicine or otherwise after the occurrence of the tooth and the matter is otherwise.
And the meaning of "the tooth is the end of treatment" is that when we used the types of remedies in a disease and those medications did not benefit, then we used lastly the tooth and it benefited; so what sense is there in saying "the tooth is the end of treatment". No to the meaning that the common people and many ignorant doctors have gone towards.
And the ancients have mentioned that the tooth made of gold is better than the one made of iron; and they said that because of the moderation of gold and the nobility of its essence, and they said it does not corrupt the place of the tooth.
Because I have tried it and found that it only does that in some bodies, not all, and the tooth made of it is better and more excellent than iron as they said; except that if you had kept the gold ingot in the fire from the beginning until the gold has been reddened.
Because it hastens to it the cold and if you increased on it in the heat it melted in the fire; and one becomes engrossed in that work so it happened that the tooth made of iron is with us faster and closer to the correct action, God willing.
And I have categorized this chapter on the tooth into sections that I have organized from head to foot so that it may be easy for the student who wants it, God willing.
The First Chapter.
In the tooth of the skull is one tooth.
This treatment is beneficial for dampness and coldness affecting the brain, which are the cause of headaches and frequent infections from the head to the eyes and ears, excessive sleepiness and toothache and throat pain. In general, for every disease that is caused by coldness such as paralysis, epilepsy, and similar types of diseases.
A picture of this treatment is for the surgeon to order first an emetic with a gentle and clean remedy for the head three nights or four, as it suits the strength of the surgeon's power and his age and habit.
Then order him to shave his head with a razor, then have him sit in front of you reclining with his hands on his chest.
Then place the tip of your finger on the tip of his nose between his eyes, and wherever you reach with your middle finger, mark that spot with ink.
Then take the oil flask whose form this is.
Expose from the bone as much as a walnut shell or a hazelnut, and raise your hand, if not then use the same file or another one until it warms up. Until you see from the bone what I have mentioned to you, then take some salt and dissolve it in water, let him drink a mouthful and apply it to the place and leave it for three days.
Then have him drink a cloth steeped in fat and leave it on him until the redness goes away from the fire, then treat him with the quadruple ointment until he recovers if God wills.
And they said that an open wound is better and more beneficial as it drains the pus.
And some of them have mentioned that the skin be cauterized to the bone and hold the cautery until some thickness of the bone is charred, then scrape off what has been charred from the bone, then treat.
Others have said that the cautery should be applied abundantly so as to affect the bone with a strong effect, until it falls from the bone like the small cirrus or a stone. They claimed that vapor of the head would rise from that place and they leave the wound open for a long time.
Then he is treated until it heals. I do not see these two types of cautery at all, except in some people and on the way of deceit. And if that happens then the head will heal when its natural connection is scattered as we have seen in all other parts.
And especially when the head of the patient is weak by nature. And I have seen that the first type of cautery is safe and better in my opinion, and if he had used it then it would be successful, God willing.

The Third Chapter.
For a congenitally united twin.
If a fissure in the head is accompanied by pain and headache which spreads to the eye, then the physician should administer purgative remedies for the head and use all other treatments mentioned in "Tasrihat al-Abd" as described. If this does not cure it, then anoint with oil on both sides. Either apply the hot quick remedy or iron.
As for applying the hot quick remedy, it is that you should take one clove of garlic, peel it and cut its ends from both sides. Then make an incision with a wide lancet in the forehead at the place of pain until there is an opening under the skin into which the garlic can be inserted.
Then the garlic should be inserted under the skin until it disappears, then tie over it with a strong bandage and leave it for as long as fifteen days, then take it out, let the wound stay for two or three days, then move.
Then tie a piece of cotton that has been soaked in fat until the area becomes inflamed, then treat it with an ointment until it heals if God wills. And if you wish to do this with some of the hot remedies I mentioned in Chapter 18 on the Hot Remedies.
And as for treating it with iron, according to this form: This is a picture of the mold shown above.
And the mold is called Samarite because its head has a twisted shape like an awl with some corrugation, and in the middle of it there is a small nail.
Then place it on the place of pain, hold your hand and turn the iron a little, a little until the amount of flesh that is burned from the thickness of the skin will be half. Raise your hand so that the artery below does not burn, causing bleeding; then soak a piece of cotton in saltwater and place it on the wound, leaving it for three days. Then carry the cotton with fat and treat it with ointment until it heals by God's will.
And if you want to clean this wound with the sharp edge of the lancet and keep it from the cut artery in this non-chronic wound only.

Make your ligature from against the diseased side because relaxation only occurs in the healthy side.
The diagram of the ligature is to make it a ligature from against the upper tip of the ear, a little under the cranium, and another on the cheekbone, its length being as long as the eyebrow.

The Eleventh Chapter.
Regarding kidney stones.
If the cause of the kidney stone is foul moisture and thick urine, cook the cauteries which we have mentioned for a patient with epilepsy.
If the cause of the kidney stone is jaundice leaning towards blackness and the patient's body is moist and foul, purify his brain as mentioned in the classification.
Then shave the patient's head and make a cake of strong flax, like a circle, then place it in the middle of his head. The patient should be seated with his back raised, holding himself on all sides. Then take one pound of old sheep fat.
Then heat it on the fire with moderate heat, until the finger can be put into it, then pour it onto the middle of his head in a circle and leave it until it cools. Do this for the patient once every week along with good treatment until he is cured if God wills.
And if you want to heat it, make many small drops without holding your hand with the cauterizing iron, but rather let it be a sprinkling, for this type of cautery moistens the brain moderately.
Then place on him a thread soaked in lard or chicken fat.
The Twelfth Chapter.
Regarding the cautery for water that has flowed into the eye.
If you find that the water flowing into the eye begins to show the signs mentioned in the classification, take care of purifying the patient's head and protecting him from all moisture and bathe him in a warm bath for several days.
Then shave his head and cook a cautery in the middle of the head, then cook two cauterizers on the temples if the water began to flow into both eyes or into one eye.
Then cut with a bone cutter all the veins and arteries under the skin, that their ligatures be as long as the width of the eyebrows.
If you see something of it, then cut it off in the manner possible and we will come with a plan for tying the arteries and cutting them and stopping the bleeding.
And he is placed in the groin under the bones two severe ligatures.

The Sixteenth Chapter.
In an eyelid mold.
If their plates are turned inside first then the mold is in two kinds within it. Either it is molded by fire or by a caustic drug, and as for molding it by fire then the operator commands that plates be left uncovered until they lengthen and even out.
If you mold it when the growths are new, tie a bandage over his eyes so that they do not move until they grow in and straighten out. If they have grown and straightened out then place the head of the operator on your lap and learn to write on the eyelid with ink an impression resembling a palm leaf.
And the mark will begin near the plates then place a cotton sponge in egg whites or in the spittle of a red pomegranate under the eyelid, and then mould this form.
Then mold it on the shape you learned a little at a time many times until the surface of the skin which is in the form of a palm leaf all of its appearance is special and the sign of the correctness of your work that you see the eyelid has become swollen and the hair has risen above the eyelid's rim.
Then lift your hand at that time and leave it for three days, then place a cotton cloth smeared with fat on it until the mold dries out, then treat it with ointment until it heals if God wills. If something of the hair returns after some time and the eyelid relaxes.
Replace the hair on that place as I have done first, if there is hair in the lower eyelid then remove it until it returns to its natural position and does not damage the eye's hair. And the bandage with the burned drug is that the operator leaves the edges alone until they lengthen and equalize.
Then make a drawing of paper mulberry and take from the usual soap and unextinguished ash each one a weight of a drachma or like it, grind them both together well and do that by mill so they don't dry. Then stretch some of it on the paper mulberry which you made in shape of mulberry leaf and put it on one or both eyelids, and put a cotton soaked in white egg under the eye and head of the operator in your hand.
And put your index finger above the medicine and compress it a little while moving it whenever the operator feels a thrill from the medicine because he finds it exciting like fire, as long as he finds the thrill leave the medicine and move it with your finger, and if the thrill calms down then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see the eyelid has risen as it rises when burned with fire or cut, otherwise reapply the medicine to the place where the medicine did not affect and did not spread until you complete your work and the eye burns then put a cloth dipped in fat on it so that the blisters of the burn go away.
Then treat it with the ointment of resin or another one until it heals, and you should be very cautious when working so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye, for if the eyelid relaxes after some days and you fear something of hair in the eye.
Then reapply the medicine to that place of the eyelid which relaxed in particular as you did first, then treat it until it heals, and this is a drawing of mulberry leaf.
Know that the eyes of people can vary in size, so according to that, your ointment should be made, and it is not advisable on someone who has a defect in this art.
The Seventeenth Chapter.
For the catarrh which appears before the eye.
If you treated the catarrh with what we mentioned in the sections of diseases and it did not cure your treatment, then take note of this quality.

It will be molded like the shape of a falcon's feather tube from one end which is for the treatment, and if you want it to be open on the other end or closed like an ointment pot, but this molded one is better for your work God willing.

And move your hand a little away from the eye towards the nose so that you do not touch it or disturb the patient, and so that the compress does not fall into the corner of the eye and cause it to become inflamed. If in the first treatment you reach the bone, but otherwise reheat the compress again if needed.

The Eighteenth Chapter.
A way of cutting a lip split.
Often a split occurs in the lip which is called the "split" and especially in the lips of children, as it often happens. If the treatment for this split mentioned in the previous section does not work, then bind to it a small heated iron thimble.
Its cavity is on the flat side of the thimble, then put it in a hot iron on the same split until the treatment reaches the depth of the split, then treat with cauterization until it heals if Allah wills.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
A way of the nasal operation which occurs in the mouth.

Chapter Twenty.
For loose teeth.
If the gums have become loose due to moisture and the canines have been treated with medicines without recovering, place the head of the drill in your palm then take the cauterizing rod which will be described after this after putting the tube on the canine.
And insert the cauterizing rod into it with a poultice on the wheel, holding your hand slightly until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth then lift your hand and repeat the cauterizing rod as you wish then fill the patient's mouth with salt water.
And hold it for an hour and then throw him, for the movable tooth will settle down and the loose gums will tighten and dry up the bad moisture.
Chapter Twenty-One.
For the pain of a loose tooth.
If the pain of a loose tooth is from cold or there are worms and the treatment with medicine has not healed, make an abscess on its two sides either the kind made with fat or the kind made with fire.
As for the abscess made with fat, it is that you take the cow's grease and boil it in an iron cauldron or a clay pot, then take a cord and wrap it around the end of the rod, then dip it into the melted fat and place it on the painful tooth with a poultice and hold it until it cools.
Then return it repeatedly until the strength of the fire reaches the root of the tooth. And if you wish to immerse a wool or cotton in cold grease and place it on the affected tooth and cover it with a protected knife until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
And as for scorching it with fire, is that you make a copper tube or an iron one and let there be some thickness in its mouth so the heat of the fire does not reach the inside of the instrument, then take out the cooled instrument which has taken shape and put it on the same tooth and hold your hand until it cools down, doing this repeatedly.
For the pain will go, either that same day or another one, and it is necessary after that scorching to fill the instrument's mouth with good fat and hold it for an hour then throw it away. And this is the shape of the instrument.
It will be shaped at whichever end you want, as best possible, and this is the shape of the tube.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
For scorching pigs.
If the pigs are stuck with mucus and cold moisture and do not bleed well with the drugs for maturity and you want quick ripening then take a hollowed out instrument shaped like this, both ends are perforated.

Then leave it for three days and place a cotton cloth soaked in fat on it until what has been burnt by the fire goes away, then treat him with ointment and cerate until he is cured, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty-Three
In the case of a swelling of the chest and narrow breathing.
If moisture has overwhelmed the trachea, especially if accompanied by a cold temperament, the physician should first give him purgative remedies to evacuate his body, then tie him with bandages in a knot in the groove of the nape at the base of the larynx.
Be careful not to reach the knot to the larynx, and do not burn the skin except half of it, then tie another knot at the neck joint in the last crease, a hump-shaped suture as mentioned before.
Then treat him according to what has been previously mentioned until he recovers if God wills.
Chapter Twenty-Fourth
In the case of the disease of the lungs and coughing.

Chapter Twenty-Fifth
In the case of a lump.

Then the skin is cauterized with it until it penetrates to the other side, and the shape of the cauterization is four cauteries. It can be cauterized with a cauterizer having three rivets in which case the shape of the cauterization will be six cauteries and the rivets are on the skin.
And this is an image of the cauterizer with three rivets.
And it can be increased from this number one, so the cauteries will be eight. Then carry on the scab with crushed dates mixed with salt and bind the patient tightly, and do not move the limb for a while until it becomes strong, and if the discharge is upwards and rarely that is the case.
Burn it with a single good hump-shaped cautery or many small ones, for the joint becomes strong and the moisture disappears and the patient recovers.

The twenty-eighth chapter.
For a swelling of the liver with jaundice.
If there is a running ulcer in the liver, and you wish to know whether this swelling is in the fat of the liver or its membranes, then if it is in the fat of the liver, the patient finds distress without great pain.
And if it is in the membrane of the liver, there will be a severe pain with it. And I have seen doctors fail to treat it, so let the patient lie on his back and learn to apply lint to the swollen place.
Then guard the pincers over the fire, which are like pliers, and this is their form. And burn it with one burn until the skin is all charred and the caustic reaches the membrane until the whole abscess comes out, then treat him with the treatment of ulcers until he recovers.
And this type of caustic should not be used except by one whose path has been long in the craft of medicine and who has practiced on him these diseases repeatedly through experience, then he may perform such an operation and leave it better with me.
The twenty-ninth chapter.
For a cauterization of the anus.
The ancients used the root of za'ran for cold hemorrhoids, and it is that you take a long dry root of za'ran as thick as a finger, then immerse it in oil and heat it in the fire. Then burn it with one caustic between the glutes and the navel, two small ones slightly tilted towards the area under the chin, and two large ones in the middle of the third and fourth ribs.
And two also between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly tilted towards the back a little, another one in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And three caustics behind, one between the shoulders, and two from the sides below the one that is between the wrists.
It is not advisable that you penetrate with your finger as much as possible, but rather be in the appearance of skin there a lump. And some of the early ones have mentioned that among people was he who used a drill made of iron almost like an awl to protect it and enter it between the ribs until it ends up reaching the tumor itself.
And the pin comes out as we have mentioned in liver tumor, and in this case from a bowel abscess either will die the operator from his fatigue or will be exposed in the place a foul-smelling discharge which will not cure.
The thirty-first part.
In the kidney.

The 32nd Chapter.
For the treatment of dropsy.

Do not deprive the patient of this treatment after applying the poultices, so that the pus accumulates and heals quickly; also note that the poultice to be applied on the back is like the previous one in shape but greenish in color.
The 23rd Chapter.
For a poultice of the feet and legs.

Then apply two poultices on the legs, one on each leg, with the sharp edge of the poultice facing downwards; one under the knee and the other below it towards the middle of the leg, and on every thigh two poultices.
Leave the poultice open without treatment for a long time to let the liquid drain from it, then treat him with what we have mentioned.

The Thirty-Fourth Chapter.

If there are in the anal region chronic fissures, many or one, and they were of thick cold mucus or foul catarrh, and it was treated with what we mentioned in the division but did not benefit from the treatment then apply to the cause three poultices on the lower back under the table slightly triangular.

The Thirty-Fifth Chapter.
In the treatment of fistulas.
After cutting it, if the fistula is cut then smear on the caustic which resembles vermilion, then insert it into the same fistula which was cut and hold your finger until the caustic reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows, do this once or twice.
If the fistulas are many, treat each one as we described then apply to them whatever ointments suit them until they heal, and if a compress on cotton was also very effective in being beneficial.
Chapter Thirty-Sixth.
In the treatment of boils which occur in the navel and its surroundings.
If the boil does not burst and the treatment we described does not work on it, perhaps the patient will recover with caustic. If one of the boils in the navel has a foul discharge and pus then the first thing you should do is to clean it with a fine spatula.
Then find out how deep it is with the spatula then smear on the caustic which resembles vermilion, then insert it into the same boil straight into the depth of the boil and where the spatula entered and repeat the caustic until those foul bodies burn up one or twice or three times according to your need.
And take care not to burn a nerve if there is one or a large vein, and if the boil bursts into the bladder or the intestines.
Take care from these places too, and do that only if the boil is in a fatty area which you have judged not to be infected, then treat the place until it heals. If the place is closed off and the matter has stopped and remained like that for some time then know that it has healed perfectly.
And if the matter does not stop coming from it then know that it is infected or there is a foul and rotten substance in its depth, or something similar that will be mentioned later in its place.

The 41st Chapter.
In a boil of elephantiasis.

Then afterwards diarrhoea and death ensued. And if the pain is on both sides stitch them in this manner.
And some of the wise scholars have mentioned a stitch for the hip, which is made in this form: they make a metal catheter half a finger in width, and it has a mouth at its thickest point or a little less, and inside that catheter there are two other catheters.
And between each of the catheters there is a space equal to that of an index finger's joint, and the catheters are open on both sides and their height is about one or two joints. And they have for it a metal handle firmly attached to the catheters, and this is its shape.
Then it is put in the fire until it becomes red and heated, then it is placed on the back of the hip and the patient reclines on the correct side. Three circular stitches are sewn at once, then he is left for three days and packed with grease, and the wound remains open for a while.
It is often used, then he is treated with ointment until it heals. The one who composed this book said: "This type of stitch was rarely practiced due to its severity and the commotion that surrounds it, and because few are those who can tolerate it. But it is a good stitch for whoever can endure it and suffers from its place.
As for cauterizing with drugs, it is to make two holes resembling the throat into which a rod of lead or iron is inserted.
There is a height of about ten in them and there is between them a thickness of the size of a finger, and they are open at the bottom and open at the top, and some have been held together like this.

Until the pain subsides, then you raise your hand with the tool and wipe away the scalding water from all of his hip with cool water, then leave him for three days and impose fat on him until the burn mark fades, and let him be for a few days until it is purged, because he will benefit greatly.
Then treat him with poultices until he recovers, and if the pain reaches his thigh or leg, make a similar apparatus for him as that which you made for his hip, either way, this is the nature of scalding water which I have proven in the Treatise on the Cure of Diseases.
You take from unheated salt and gypsum a part from each, crush them, then put them in a new vessel which has been pierced at the bottom with a small hole like the size of a reed, and place under the bottom of the vessel another mixed quantity.
Then pour cool water on the salt and gypsum so that it covers them with a finger, after you have grasped them well with your hand, then leave the vessel until scalding water descends into the lower mixed vessel, then gather all of that hot water and pour it over another new gypsum and salt again.
Indeed, it becomes very sharp in that state and performs many medical actions and operations on various parts of the body because it does exactly what fire does. Among its medicines is something that also strengthens the loins, such as thapsia, honey of dates palm tree, and clay mixed with soap crushed finely.

Until he may go into the bath while being carried and come out cured, by taking some of the green chicory then if the green is not found take the fresh one and pound it with a bit of fat and put it on the loins where the pain is or in the leg or in the thigh.
It is applied and left for as long as three hours or until the patient feels a quieting of the pain, then he is taken to the bath. If his body needs it, he is put in the pool, because the pain goes away and he is cured with God's permission. If he is not cured, the poultice is reapplied on him after ten days again.

The poultice will be in this form, wool is taken and soaked in old oil and put on the deep place which is between the wrist of the hand and the elbow, closer to the elbow then take the dried fat of a goat.
So it is heated over the fire until it becomes a glowing ember then put it on the wool and leave it until it cools down, then take another one and continue doing that until the sensation reaches the middle of the arm to the loins and the pain calms down with God's permission. This type of poultice is called the fat poultice.
The 42nd Chapter.
For the treatment of back pain.
The back pain may result from many causes, such as a fall or blow, or excessive vomiting and the like. And it may be caused by an accumulation of cold moist matter; this treatment is specifically for that type.
The patient should be made to vomit with a warm paste, and then the cupping glass is placed on his back where the pain is, three rows of it, on the same surface of the table, after the area has been marked with ink in each row five or more cups according to how much the doctor sees from the patient's capacity and strength.
And the cup may be with a single point cupping needle, or if you wish three or four concave cupping needles of medium size in this shape.
The 43rd Chapter.
For the treatment by cupping at the beginning of a boil.
This affliction often occurs in small children, and a sign that it has begun is when the child finds difficulty breathing on exerting himself or moving about, and at the end of his backbone you will find a knot which has appeared and stands out more than other knots.
If you see that and want to stop it, cup with a ring-shaped cupping needle of this shape. To take the cupping on every side of the lump evenly, and if you wish to cup around the lump with a single point cupping needle in two or three rows, with the points close together. Then treat the area until it clears up as we mentioned.
And be careful not to use cupping for a boil that is caused by inflammation of the nerve.

For treating gout and pains in the joints.

And if it becomes necessary to apply a poultice on the face of the leg, do so with a pustule poultice. And if the pains have risen to the knees or to other joints, and this often happens, then apply on every knee three or four poultices from each side with that same olive oil poultice.
And if you need more than this poultice, apply it without inserting your hand into the poultice, but rather so that it is on top of the skin about as thick as a finger. And if the pains have risen to the hips or to the back, then use what we mentioned from the poultice in its place.

The Forty-Fifth Chapter.
In a poultice for boils.
If an abscess is shown in the groin and some of the pus and matter have descended to the testicles and that is beginning, it is advisable that the doctor order him to abstain from eating for a day and to use some purgative to evacuate his belly.

Then protect this cauldron with its shape.
Until it comes out white, then put the cup or syringe into it. Then a servant puts his hand on the place so that the cup will not protrude. It has been removed between the patient's legs and placed under him, with another servant tightening his legs.
And another on his chest holding his hands then the cauldron is lowered onto the same mark and your hand with the cauldron upright firmly hold it until it reaches the bone or return to its place if it did not reach the bone at first.
And be careful not to let the cup protrude while cauterizing lest it burns him, and as a result the patient will either die or suffer severe damage. Know that if you did not reach the bone with your cauterization then your treatment was unsuccessful. But if you burn a part of the skin like a third of it, then treat it as we mentioned; God willing, it will not increase. Chapter Forty-eight.
In the case of a clubbing (of fingers).
If there occurs a loss or blow, with pain and duration for a long time, and the treatment by medicine does not relieve it, then one should cauterize the point with a mallet, and the shape of every member should be according to its size, smallness, weakness, and strength.
And if the pain and swelling are relieved from it, then he is cured of the first cauterization. Otherwise, return to cauterize him again because it is the nature of these pains that they move from one member to what is near to it, so follow them with cauterization until the patient is healed.
Chapter Forty-nine.
In the case of a leper's cauterization.
But the lepers can benefit from cauterization with great benefit, especially in the case of scrofula where the phlegm and blackness have become dry.

And know that the leper does not feel pain from the compress as a healthy person would because his body is numb, and it should be so with the compresses of old age and youth according to the characteristics of the bandages mentioned earlier.

The 48th Chapter.
In the compress of numbness, when an organ has become numb and was treated with medicines and ointments and dressings but did not recover, then treat the same organ itself with compresses according to what its bone deserves in terms of size or density. Let your compress be made of linen and fat a little thin.
Then treat it with ointment until he recovers. It may be that some numbness comes out on the hand and leg in the clefts of the back when the nerve going to move that member is cut off.
And he should not proceed with that except from one who is well aware of the anatomy of the members and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
The Forty-Ninth Chapter.
For Scabies.
If the scabies advances and no trick of medicine helps him, then treat it in depth a little bit according to the thickness of the skin so that the whiteness goes away and its colour changes.
Then treat it with fine vermiform powder, mixed with the red of madder and the sap of the papyrus plant or the blood of the leeches, from one part each, all mixed together and applied to a cloth, and bind the place until he recovers.
The Fiftieth Chapter.
For Tumour Treatment.
If the tumour is new and you want to prevent it, apply a burning iron to it around as it turns. And some wise men have said that one should treat it with a severe medicine inside it, but I do not think so because I expect it to ulcerate and I have seen that happen several times.
The correct thing is to treat its edges with a burning iron around, as we said, or with many dressings.
The Fifty-First Chapter.
For Carbuncle Treatment.
If a carbuncle has occurred in one of them and it has been delayed in its growth either due to the effective cause or due to the age of the patient being old and lacking blood, or due to time, and you want to hasten its growth, treat around it with many small dressings sprinkled.
Then leave it alone, for it will heal quickly. If you wish to dry it with the hot iron, have the iron in this shape.
And place it in the middle of the emery until the skin perforates, and let the iron be below so that it is easy to remove the filth, then treat it as needed until it heals.
The 52nd Chapter.
Regarding the hot iron for eating.
The eater is a corruption that seeks in the body to consume it, just as fire consumes dry wood. If you see the eater in a place where it can be consumed by fire, apply many small and large smears of hot iron according to what suits that place in which the eater is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until the corruption is completely eliminated and nothing remains. Then leave it for three days and apply to the burned areas sulfur powder mixed with oil until the blisters break out and all the corruption comes out.
Then treat it with medicated ointments for the flesh. If you see after three days that the flesh is sprouting a healthy growth without corruption in it, otherwise reapply the cauterization to what remains of the corrupt areas, and the eater can be treated with purgative medicine.
For it serves as a substitute with fire in being more effective, and I have mentioned its treatment with purgative medicine in the section, so take it from there when you need it.
The 53rd Chapter.
Regarding the cauterizing of nails that are bent and not bent.
Often this affliction occurs in the soles of the feet, it is a rough thing that torments the man, and treatment for it is by cauterizing with fire or with hot water.
As for cauterizing, it is to prepare a metal catheter resembling the tail of an eagle, made of iron according to the size that fits around the reed, with thin edges. Then place the catheter over the reed and turn your hand holding the catheter around the reed until the catheter reaches the depth of the reed.
And leave it for three days until it suppurates, then tie it with dampened herbal compresses that have been kneaded with salt. Leave the dressing overnight and it will come out from its roots, then treat the wound place with a salve made to promote flesh until it heals, if the splinters are not rotated.
And often it occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet. It is necessary to take a tube from copper or iron or from the eagle's feather, place it over the splinter or abscess, then pour into the tube a little boiling water.
And grasp your hand as you turn it slightly with a little flexing of the fingers so that the edge of the tube affects the base of the splinter. The boiling water will find its way to penetrate into the base of the splinter and cause the patient some pain for about an hour.
Then leave it, for the splinter will come out with its roots. You do this one by one until you reach all of it in the body, then treat its places after they have come out with a salve made to promote flesh.
The Fourth and Fifty-second Chapter.
In cauterizing the suppurating abscess.
If a suppurating abscess has occurred in one of the nerves due to cold or quartan fever, or something else, it is necessary to cauterize it four or five times on the vertebrae between each vertebra and in its chest. On his abdomen with the oil-iron cautery that the scab falls and the cold sickness heals quickly.
The fifty-second chapter.
On a boil which has occurred in the body.
It may burst in the body with ugly boils that are due to thick, rotten cold matter. It is necessary at first appearance to cauterize on top of each boil with a gentle cautery stick, or the tip of a reed which has been lit, or with a long piece of al-zarawand wood, or with an olive-sized iron cautery.
And the swellings may cauterize at their first burst in this manner, and they will not increase or become inflamed, nor will there be a stain from them, except that it is necessary for the cause to be bled first.
The sixty-sixth chapter.
On a bleeding which has occurred when the artery has been cut.
A haemorrhage often occurs from an artery that has been cut when a wound is made which exposes it from outside, or when an abscess is opened or the ligature of a member is cauterized and its like.
If it happens to one of them, then hasten with your hand to the mouth of the artery and place your thumb on it firmly until the blood is stopped under your thumb and nothing comes out from it, then you place small and large olive-sized cauteries in the fire and breathe on them until they are very hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large according to the wound and the place where the artery has burst open, and put the cautery on the same spot after you have removed your thumb with a gentle pull and held the cautery until the blood stops.
If the bleeding bursts forth when you remove your thumb from the artery and the cautery has gone out, then take another one quickly with a spatula from the hot olive-sized cauteries that are prepared in the fire, and continue to do this one after another until the blood stops.
Do not burn the wood when you have to cut again. Know that if an artery is bleeding, it cannot be stopped or, especially, cut off unless through one of four methods: either by cauterizing as we have said, or by amputating it, provided it has not been severed already. If it is amputated, the two ends will constrict and the bleeding will stop. It can be bound tightly with threads or remedies placed on it which are intended to cut off the bleeding and tighten it strongly with bandages.
And as for someone who tries to cut it with a band or by pulling tight with a ligature, or by placing burnt things and so on, it does not stop at all in most cases. But if one of those occurs and there is no doctor nor medicine then let him quickly place the index finger into the wound itself as we have described.
And he should hold it tight very much until the bleeding ceases and stops from above the wound. And on the artery and finger, cold water should not be removed from them always making the blood congeal and thicken and stop. And in that meanwhile, one looks at what is needed of cauterization or medicine.
The Second Chapter.
Concerning the incision, cut, and venesection, and similar wounds.

Therefore, a warning should be included that is stronger, since the surgery in this matter often results in bleeding of the blood with which life exists when an artery is opened or incision is made on a tumor or abscess or surgical treatment or removal of an arrow or cut for stone and so forth that accompanies most of them are peril and fear and death occurs in most of them.
And I advise you to beware of falling into what is ambiguous, for it may occur to you in this craft types of people with kinds of ailments, so some of them have grown tired of their illness and are weary of death.
Because of the severity of his illness and the length of his suffering, and because his ailment indicates that death is near, some of them will offer you their money in order to be cured, and they will exert themselves for your sake, expecting a cure from their sickness, so it does not behove you to assist any of those who have this characteristic whatsoever.
And may your caution be even stronger than your eagerness and desire, and you should not proceed with anything of this sort unless it is with certain knowledge that will lead to a praiseworthy outcome for you, and you should employ in the treatment of all your patients the superiority of knowledge and warning them of what leads to safety.
For in that there is a help for you to acquire praise and glory, remembrance and thanks, may God guide you with His wisdom and not deprive you of correctness and success, for that is in His hand, no god except Him.
And I have treated this matter in sections to the extent that was mentioned earlier in the chapter on the art of the ancient ages so that it is easier for you to understand what you want from it, God willing.

In the treatment of water that accumulates in the heads of boys.

And I have seen a boy whose head was filled with water, and his head grows larger every day. Until the boy could not bear to sit up on account of the swelling of his head and the moisture increases until he died.
And this moisture is either among the skin and bone, or under the bone on the peritoneum. The operation for that, if the moisture is between the skin and bone, and the swelling is small, is to make a cut in the middle of the head, one incision from front to back, until the moisture flows out. This is the shape of the instrument used.
If the moisture increases and the swelling grows greater, then make two intersecting cuts like this shape:.
And if the moisture is under the bone, and its sign is that you see the scalp sutures opened from all sides, and the water lowers when you press it with your hand into it, rather than on top of it, then make three cuts in the middle of the head like this shape.
And after the cut, all the moisture comes out, then the incisions are sewn with thread and papyrus, and it is wrapped from above with a paste and oil until the fifth day, then the bandage is removed and the wound is treated with lint and ointments. When one experiences a sudden affliction to the eyes or chest, and treatment by medication was ineffective, then the cure in that case is cutting these two arteries.

The blood will flow in a quantity of six dirhams, or more or less, all of that according to the strength of the patient and the filling of his arteries. Then you should look at the wound; if there remains anything from the flesh on the bone, cut it off.
So that a hot tumor may not appear; then tie the wound with a thread from linen cloth, and treat it with ointments until it heals.
The third chapter.

The blades of the instrument are sharp like small knives except they are much less sharp, for if they were as sharp as a knife they would quickly become cold and fail to cut the flesh quickly. So, if there is some thickness in them, warm fire clings to it.
And cut the flesh quickly. This is better than any work, and it is lighter and easier; let there be a space of the thickness of a finger between the blades.

The Eighth Chapter.
In the treatment of swellings that appear on the eyelid.

The Ninth Chapter.
Treatment of the inflammation in the eyelids.
Often a thing similar to ice in its hardness and softness is exposed on the eyelid.

Then remove it gently from all sides until it is cleaned, then clamp it with a pincer and cut it. If you are unable to cut it unless the eyelid is perforated by the cut, this will not harm the growth at all; if the incision is large, sew it up and treat it until it heals.
And if it is small, there is no harm from it; for the ointment will hold it and protect it. And if the ice is turned towards the inside of the eyelid towards the inner surface, then invert the eyelid and clamp the ice with a pincer without cutting, and remove it from all sides.
And if the eyelid is perforated by the cut, that will not harm anything; then wash the eye with salty water after cutting off the ice and treat the place with what consolidates until the growth heals.
The Tenth Chapter.
In the treatment of cataract which presents itself in the eyelid.
Cataract is a growth which occurs in the upper layers of the eyelid, and it most often presents itself in children, weighing down their eyes and exposing them to colds, so that they are unable to look at the light of the sun. So that tears rush towards them.
And therefore you find them always leaning on their faces and sleeping with it, and their eyelids under the eyebrows are wet and puffed up; and if you press the place with your fingers, you will feel the cataract between them. The treatment is that the doctor should put his head against yours.
Then you take a piece of cotton cloth and prepare an awl from it, then make a circle with the awl as large as will enclose the cataract on all sides, then place it on him and press with your fingers on all sides to gather the cataract in the center of the circle.
Then you make a cut with a scalpel in the middle of that moisture, making it as long as possible without making it wider than the incision for the drainage, but when cutting deeper it is necessary to cut all the skin until reaching the cataract.
In most cases, the cataract will protrude from the incision in the form of a white piece of fat which you should pick up with a cloth that you have wrapped around your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is freed, and beware not to increase the incision lest the scalpel touch the eye and cause harm.
If the cataract does not appear to you in the first incision, it is necessary that you increase the incision a little bit gently until the cataract appears, then pull it out as we said, and then dip a cloth into vinegar and water and place it on the place and bandage it, and some people crush salt on it.
Place it in the cavity of the incision so that what remains of moisture may dissolve, then treat him until he is clean. If an abscess or a hot swelling occurs in the place, treat him with embrocations smeared with unguents until he is clean.

And the lower eyelid may also be exposed that its lashes turn over, it is necessary to use in this what we have mentioned from cutting and stitching and scorching with fire and applying a hot medication, or scorching with fire or applying a hot medication more effective and lighter on the lid than cutting and stitching.
The cleansing with papyrus is of this kind, that you turn up the eyelid and cut the incision from inside as I have described, then make two or four small strips lengthwise on the eyelid, thinner than the blade.
And I have tied them to each end where the threads cling, then joined them gently on what is left of the eyelid and tightened the strips from both sides tightly and let it for some days; for the pulled skin will die and turn black and rot.
Until it falls from itself; if I delayed, I have bandaged it with linen then treated it until it healed. If the eyelid stuck together and the lashes of the eye did not become numb, this is the shape and quantity of the strips in length and width.
The Twelfth Chapter.
For raising the protruding hairs from the eye with a needle.
If it were a hair or two, the work is that you take a thin needle and insert into it a thread of fine silk which has been smoothed then tie both ends together tightly in a very delicate knot; let its length be around one finger's breadth.
Then tie another thin thread over it in the knot and tie its ends if you wish, then put the needle's head into your palm, let it be near the sun so the work will be clear; for it is delicate work. Then insert the needle with the knot into the root of the protruding hair.
And execute it in the eyelid with a gentle touch until it comes out above the natural hair, then pull the thread up to above the knot and insert into that knot the protruding hair if it is one or two or three at most.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the knot in the eyelid along with the natural hair; if you pulled the thread and the hair did not come out with it, then pull the thread down with the knot which was tied around it until the knot comes out from the upper hole.
Then you put the hair back in and pull it up, so that it protrudes from the upper hole as far as the eye can see. Then remove the forceps and thread and leave the eyelid tightly tied for two or three days until the hair grows on its place and flesh forms over it.
If the hair is short, then either add to it a long hair from natural hair so that they rise together, or else leave it until it grows longer after a period of time; then raise it.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of swelling that occurs in the upper eyelid of the eye.
Which is exposed to this swelling is called Arnebia and it can be either natural or secondary; the secondary one being from the effusion of a wound or cut or boil, etc.
And the procedure in it is to cut through that effusion and spread its edges and place a thread of linen between them and tie it until it heals, nor should you use things that dry up and contract for its treatment.
If you did that, the swelling will return worse than it was; but use in its treatment moistened things like ointments and pastes such as soap with henna or safflower mixed with something of paint to stain the cloth.
And the key to its treatment is to try by all means not to become stuck in the shape it was originally, and this procedure which we mentioned is only a repair of the swelling and not for the place to return exactly as it was from the beginning.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of swelling that occurs in the lower eyelid.
This swelling that occurs from the conjunctiva is what is called a pterygium and it can be either natural or secondary; the secondary one being from a wound or cut or boil, etc.
The way of operation in this is to take a needle with two threads and insert it into the flesh and draw it out from the left aperture to the right aperture until the thread is at the ends of the flesh. Then extend the flesh upwards by the needle and cut it with a broad scissors.
If the shape of the fold returns as it should, otherwise take a forceps and place it on the site of the cut, turn with it the fold, and make two cuts in the inner side of the fold, and be the edges of the cuts until they meet so that there is an angle. Until it meets the shape becomes similar to this shape:.
And it is the Greek letter alpha, then remove that flesh as much as the sharp edge from below the fold. Then gather the scattered parts with two stitches and sew him with a woolen thread, then treat him with what we have mentioned of remedies and fat until he heals.
And if the slit is open from a cut or stitch or skin, it should be cut with a simple cut without also the hairs of the eyelashes as mentioned above, then spread between the lips with fat as we have mentioned.
And in summary, the treatment of a slit whether from above or below is to do whatever work becomes available to you according to the appearance of the slit, since it may be variously different in shape. The craftsman makes provision for the trick however he can.
Until its shape returns to its natural form or approximates it, and the same illness guides you to what is suitable for him from the work and the tool in most cases.
Chapter Fifteen.
For the adhesion of the eyelid to the eyebrow or to the corner.
This adhesion may be exposed to many people that the upper eyelid adheres to the white of the eye preventing it from moving easily and hindering its natural actions, so it is necessary to insert the end of a forceps under the eyelid.
Hold it up above or grasp it with a spatula, then cut the adhesion with a gentle, not forceful, needle cutting motion, so that the needle does not cause alarm to the patient and comes loose in his eye causing damage by its sharpness. Cut like peeling away that adhesion.
Then wait until the eyelid returns to its natural state and all adhesion is gone, then pour into the eye a salty water to wash it with or drop therefrom a solution of zinc antimony dissolved in water. Then spread between the eyelid and eye with a cotton thread.
And place on top of the eye a wool soaked in egg white, and after three days use the antimony solution until it clears.
Chapter Sixteen.
For cutting the stylophora (or nail plate) and peeling the epidermis of the finger nails.
The stylophora is of two kinds, either it will be firm and fibrous resembling a hard, thin stick, or it will be non-fibrous resembling a cold, white moisture which when touched with iron or grasped with the spatula will be cut.
And it will not remain in the spatula, and both types begin from the larger fold until they slightly spread out to cover the sight and prevent light and eye movement, and the operation of cutting it is that the patient places his head on your lap.
Then he opens his eyes and raises the eyelid with your hand, then pick up the stylophora with a gentle curved spatula and extend it upwards, then take a needle and insert a strand of horse or cow hair and a strong thread into it, bend the tip of the needle slightly and thrust it into the middle of the stylophora.
And push it through with the needle, tie the stylophora with the thread and extend it upwards and peel off with the hair one side of the stylophora which is next to the pupil as if you are spreading it with the hair until the end, then cut the rest at the root of the fold with a gentle lancet or small scissors and leave the natural epidermis.
Indeed, he must not expose the part which has a continuous flow of blood. The cut should be sutured alone or with a thread as we have mentioned, then the end which is shown in this figure should be peeled off with a smooth scraper.
It should be guarded against having the scraper touch the conjunctiva, so a cleft may occur in it and the lacrimal gland become inflamed. Then after cutting, something of powdered salt or of zanjbar's powder is put into the eye, left until another day, then treated as required until it clears up.
If the cut is not irritable and no needle can be inserted into it or a needle cannot be fixed in it, this type of cut is often treated with medicine so that it clears up as I described in the partition. And if you want to cut it, open the eye of the patient.
Take a smooth scraper weak at its edge on this shape:. Scrape the cut with it gently from above, scraping only, if you see that it breaks apart and disperses, put into the eye from your hourglass some zanjbar's powder or red iron filings or powdered salt and close the eye until another day.
Then repeat the operation on it until all of them go away, unless a hot boil appears in the eye, leave it and treat the hot boil until it clears up then repeat the operation on it with the scraper until it clears up. And as for hanging flesh from the socket.
If the hanging flesh is injuring the eye severely, tie that hanging flesh with a needle and cut some of it, without lingering in cutting lest bleeding occurs then scatter red iron filings or zanjbar's powder into the sockets until it clears up.
Chapter Seventeen.
On cutting ingrowing hair and that which grows from excessive flesh in the eye.
Some people may grow red flesh in their eyes, accumulated until it covers the appearance or approaches or overflows onto the eyelids, and perhaps the eyelids have turned outwards and resemble a rose of jasmine.
And the procedure for it is that the physician places his head in the patient's armpit then opens his eyes and catches that red flesh all together with suitable tweezers.
Or he seizes it with a needle or spatula then cuts the first piece of flesh, one after another until it is all cut up and preserved from the eye lest it harm it when working, and your cutting for him may be either with a fine razor that we have described in cutting an ingrown nail or with a small scissor. In the manner you catch hawps with it as shown in the chapter which is in this chapter.
If your cutting has been done and all the redness has gone, then fill the eye with ground salt or crush in it red powder and similar potent remedies and place on the eye from outside a compress of white cloth to secure the hot swelling.
If there remains something of the redness and it flows with blood and you fear the hot swelling, then leave the eye alone and treat it with what will calm the swelling then return to it with the operation until it clears up, and do likewise for the excess flesh that is exposed in the eye from this kind.
But it is necessary for you to avoid treating every weak eye by the method of the iron instrument or from the manifest cause by working with it until you see that that organ is capable of this operation.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
In removing hawps from the eye.
Hawps are red veins that form on the eye preventing vision, and weaken the eye with time. You should first inspect it, if the eye in which hawps have formed is strong and there is no other disease besides hawps.
When this is the case, then tell the patient to place his head in your lap. Then tie the veins with a single or double thread according as you deem best, and the threads should be soft and pliable in that form.
Or there should be two intertwined threads in one body, like this form.
Then catch the veins with a gentle scissors, gently and from time to time wipe out blood until you see that the eye is freed of those veins and the bleeding has stopped. And take care not to hurt the eye with the ends of the scissors. Do this work in the middle of the day facing the sun.
And hold steady in your work so as not to cut anything but those veins. When you are finished, insert into the eye the green or red needle to eat up what is left from the arteries. If this is impossible for you, then compress the eye with whatever will soothe the pain of the eye.
And leave it for a few days until the pain subsides and the warm swelling disappears. Then repeat the operation on it in the same manner until this appearance of the needle is gone from it.
And leave it [and the patient's head will be in the student's lap and another one will wipe away the tears and inspect the anterior part of the eye and its posterior part]  and the original operation is to open the eye with openings that are fixed or triangular, which a student holds.
He is careful and the patient's head will be in the student's lap, and another one wipes away the tears and inspects the anterior part of the eye and its posterior part by choice that you begin the ligation from the upper eyelid or from its lower part. The first is that two threads are ligated on the upper lid, one at the end of it and the other at the beginning.
Then you hold them between the eyebrows and cheeks, then tie threads underneath them, then hold them between the canthi and orbita. Then draw out your hand gently until you see all the veins have risen; cut from the smaller one with the scissors or a soft forceps.
A patient with a severe injury should be treated on a cloth-covered wooden board and all the limbs should be straightened until he is raised above the bed, without cutting the bandages. Then his tears and blood will cease.
Then cut with the pincers what exceeds the bandages from above and from below until nothing remains except in the groin. If you can lift him up on the groin, remove with the razor, for it is better and may heal in some people.
If you cut him, he would experience a discharge of pus for several days, suffering from pain and swelling around the wound. Then redress the wound again.
Chapter Nineteen.
For the treatment of a splinter under the nose.
The physicians call this splinter a "nasura". If it is treated with the caustic or the hot remedy mentioned above and does not heal, then there is no remedy for it except to incise on the boil when it becomes ripe and extract all the moisture inside it or the pus.
Until the bone is exposed. If the bone becomes exposed and you see in it decay or blackness, then cut it with this instrument.
And it is called the "head of the steel" which is made from Indian iron and its head is twisted like a file, one can engrave on it a fine mark like that of a rasp or an escapel. Then put it on the place of decay from the bone and turn it between your fingers while you moisten your hand a little until you know that that decay has been cleaned out.
And you do that several times, then cauterize the place with dried adhesive remedies. If the wound has been closed and flesh has grown in it and the flow of pus has stopped and it has remained for forty days without getting worse or breaking out again, and no accident has occurred in it.
Therefore, know that it has healed. Otherwise, there is no remedy for it except to return the nasura to the nostril's hole in this manner and this is by exposing the bone again with iron or the hot remedy. If the bone becomes exposed, take a twig like this:.
Its handle should be triangular and the end of its head cone-shaped, curved towards itself as you see. Then place it on the bone itself near the joint and a little farther from the eye than your hand, then turn your hand with the instrument until it penetrates the bone and the surgeon feels it.
He should find air coming out of it if he puts his hand on its nozzle. Then, when the place is compressed with dried adhesive medicines as I have taught you, if the flesh swells and the place becomes hard then the matter that was directed to the outside will return into the nostril, and that will be easier for the surgeon, God willing.
Chapter Twenty.
A reed for the eye.
If the eye swells with its contents and does not cause an affliction or a defect in sight, it is incumbent upon the surgeon to ease it then remove it from the socket and put a plug in the socket without requiring anything else and then take out a thin cloth.
Then she puts a compress on the eye made from rosewater, myrrh, and aloeswood then pulls the eye upwards towards the compress with great benefit. The recipe for the compress is that you should take many thin cloths, fold each one in four folds and make many of them.
Then she puts one on top of the other on the eye as much as it needs then pulls a strong cloth over it and repeats the plug with the same cloth without requiring anything else, then removes the plug and leaves the eye swollen for a day and night.
If the bandage loosens during that time, it is incumbent upon her to pull tight again. Then remove the bandage after a day and night as we said. If you see the eye has returned to its normal state, but if not then repeat the compress and the compress cloth, the pulling and the plug until it returns.
Chapter Twenty-One.
In cutting the spleen.
If a rent appears in the splenic layer then it becomes swollen and protrudes outside the peritoneum like an unripe pomegranate, its form being hideous on account of this and you wish to cut it. The procedure for doing so is as I have described.
And this is that you insert a needle into the base of the pomegranate from below to above, then insert another needle into it with a doubled thread from the direction of the incision and complete it, leaving the first needle as it is.
Then cut the place of the doubling of the thread and tie some of the pomegranate around the needle with it, then pull it tight. Then withdraw the needle and put a wool moistened in egg white on the eye. Let it be until the threads fall off along with the pomegranate, then treat the eye as strengthens it.
Until the wound heals, and you may tighten the pomegranate from all sides with a circle of a cloth so that the eye becomes more swollen. Then apply a thin sponge that reaches to the bottom of the eye and releases egg white moisture and the eye descends and softens in place then tighten it until it heals.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
In the treatment of a hernia.
This is the affliction called a hernia, which is a swelling in the eye resembling falling water that has no water, and the procedure for it is that you make the patient sit on a raised chair then take their head with your hands from both sides.
And move him until you see the swelling go down below with your eyes, then hold it and it does not budge, and vision returns and the patient can see things as they were. And if it did not descend below as we mentioned, know that it is water, and if it was not ready to descend as described.
And otherwise, sit the patient in front of you then take a thin sponge and split it slightly above the conjunctival membrane where the eyelid joins the conjunctival membrane at the corner of the eye until the swelling comes out.
If only water had come out of the eye, then warm water mixed with aloe or water that has been heated with gum acacia and aloe should be applied, and other remedies should be treated until it heals.
The Twenty-Third Chapter.

It is necessary that the cup should go as far as the depth of the cup to the point where it reaches the corner of the eye, and this is from the white part to the end of the black. The Twenty-Fourth Chapter.
For the treatment of the flesh which grows in the nose.
It may grow in the nose flesh of various kinds, some of which resemble many-legged scorptions and some of it is cancerous, hard and dark in colour, and some of it is soft and not dark.
But if it is soft and not malignant, the surgeon should sit facing the sun, open his nostrils, and insert the catheter into that flesh then pull it out, then cut with a sharp pointed instrument what he has extracted from there.
Until you know that all the flesh has gone, if some of it remains which you were unable to cut, remove it with one of the smooth instruments gently until none remains. If blood or a hot pustule appears.
Then treat him as is proper, or if it was from the malignant boils, then be quick to cauterize until the blood stops and all the flesh goes away, then insert in the nose after cutting a mixture of vinegar and water or drink, in case the nostril opens and moisture flows into the throat.
Then know that he has recovered, and if the moisture does not flow as it should then know that there is flesh growing inside the vertebrae which the instrument could not reach with the cut, so at that time it is necessary to take a cotton thread with some thickness.
And tie many knots in it, and make between each knot the amount of a finger or less, then the surgeon inserts one end of the thread into his nose with a spoon or what he can use after making it like a quill, and draws out its smell until it reaches the pharynx.
He brings it out of his nostril, and the children often do this action while playing, which is an easy thing for one who wills it. Then the ends of the thread are gathered, one end that has come out by the mouth and the other that remains in the nostril.
Then the flesh is separated by the knot on the thread until one knows that the flesh has been cut with the knot of the thread. Then the thread is removed and inserted into the nostril after cleaning it, a thread which was soaked in the ointment should be done for three days or more.
Until the ointment is eaten by all that remains of the flesh. Then the last thing in the nostril becomes a lead tube for some days until it heals, if it needs treatment, I used this.

Chapter Twenty-Five.
In the abscesses that have formed at the tip of the nose.
Often a boil grows at the end of the nose, it becomes large and increases with the days until its appearance is ugly.

But if the tumour is soft to the touch and pale in color, as I have observed, then you can remove the entire thing. The twenty-sixth chapter.
In the suturing of the nose, cheek and ear. If its connection is severed due to a wound or something similar, know that whenever this happens the reconnection will be difficult in one of these membranes and the surgery will rarely succeed except in some people.

The twenty-seventh chapter.
In the removal of the swelling that appears in the lips.

Chapter Twenty-eight.
For cutting excess flesh in the mouth.
Often there is excess flesh growing on the gum, which the ancients called apulis. It should be attached to a needle or held with a probe and cut at its root and the site left to bleed then powdered alum put on it.
or one of the fibrous polyps, when it is dried. If that flesh returned after treatment, often it returns again, cut it a second time and eat it because it will not return afterwards.
Chapter Twenty-nine.
For extracting teeth with iron.
There can be rough, ugly scales in the surfaces of the teeth from inside and outside and between the gums. They may turn greenish, yellowish or black until they spread to the gum and spoil the teeth making them ugly.
Then you should sit the surgeon in front of you and his head close to your cheek and remove the molar and tooth that shows him the scales and the thing like sand until nothing is left. And do the same with the yellow, green, black and other colors until it is clean.
If what is inside comes out on the first extraction, otherwise you should repeat the extraction another day and another and another until your goal is achieved. And know that the molar needs a different type of extraction with various shapes according to what suits your work.
In order that the root of a tooth be extracted from within by means other than the one which is used to extract it from outside and the one which is used between the teeth in another shape, these many shapes of extracting it will be prepared for you all.
The Thirty-Second Chapter.
In Tooth Extraction.
It is advisable to treat the root of the tooth gently and not to extract it hastily, for there may be another good reason behind it if you do so.
If the operator is resolved to extract it, then the tooth and its root should be well stabilised. Often the operator is deceived by the root and thinks it to be in a healthy tooth, so he extracts it, then the unhealthy tooth does not go until its root is extracted.
If the tooth and its root are healthy with it, then you should bind around the tooth with a thread that has some strength in it so that the gums may be freed from all sides and then you should move it gently with your fingers or with soft forceps little by little until you shake it.
Then the two forceps can be taken hold of firmly and the head of the operator will place his hands between his knees, where he may have steadied himself so that they shall not move. Then draw out the tooth straightly lest you break it. And if the tooth is perforated or split, it should be filled with a cloth and then securely tied with a thin thread so that it does not come out when you grip it with forceps. It should also be freed from around the gums in all directions, yes.
Be careful not to overexert yourself lest you break and it returns on the patient with a worse injury than the first, and do not act as those foolish surgeons in their bridge-building and their rushing into fortification without employing what we have described.
Many times they inflict great injuries on people, easier than breaking a tooth and leaving its roots all or part of it. The 24th Chapter.
On the swelling that arises on another part.
The swellings, if they arise on a part other than their natural place, are ugly in that form, especially among women and slaves. If the swelling has arisen from behind another tooth it should be looked at.
