And if a tooth has cracked and is causing the tongue pain when speaking, then it should also be cooled until the tenderness of that crack goes away and becomes even and smooth so that it does not cause pain to the tongue or muddle speech.
The 33rd Chapter.
On bridging the movable teeth with threads of silver or threads of gold.
If the front teeth become loose and move with a blow or fall, and the patient cannot grasp anything to eat lest they fall, and having treated them with binding medicines the treatment did not cure.
The trick is to pull with a thread of gold or silver, and gold is better because silver rusts and rots after some days, while gold remains in the same state forever and does not corrode. The thread should be intermediate in thickness and fineness according to what is between the teeth.
Picture of the suture: Take a thread and insert its bend between the two healthy teeth, then sew with both ends of the thread into one or more mobile teeth until you reach the healthy tooth from the other side.
Then return the suture to its initial side and hold your hand gently and wisely until it does not move at all, and make sure the thread's tension is on the roots of the teeth so that it will not come loose. Then cut the ends of the clean thread with scissors, join them together and twist them together with a thread holder and hide them between the healthy tooth and the mobile tooth.
So that the tongue does not get injured, then leave it like this tautly as long as there is a part left. If it loosens or breaks, tighten it with another thread and enjoy it like this all day. This is the picture of the teeth and the condition of the suture in two healthy teeth and two mobile teeth as you see:.
And the single tooth or both can return to their place after they fall and be sutured as we described and remain, but only a skilled craftsman can do that. And he may carve a bone from cattle bones and make it in the shape of a tooth and put it in the place where the tooth went out. And he tightens it as we said, then it remains and he enjoys that.
Chapter Thirty-Four.
In cutting the ligament which is exposed under the tongue in those who prevent speech.
This ligament that is exposed under the tongue may either be a natural one with which man is born or an accessory one from a wound that has healed.
And the procedure for it is that you open the patient's mouth and his head in your lap, raise his tongue, then cut the nerve ligament with a sharp instrument until the tongue moves freely from its hold. If there is some hardness and complication in it and it was caused by a healed wound, poke into it with an awl and cut it carefully with a sharp instrument until the ligament softens and the knot unravels.
Be on guard lest the incision be too deep, thus cutting through blood vessels there and causing haemorrhage. Then compress with rosewater or vinegar and cold water in place of the wound. At night put a wick of flax under the tongue that the attendant may grasp it throughout the night.
Lest it become stuck together again; if bleeding occurs, place on the spot zaja powdered. If blood overpowers you, bind the area with a bandage of bean size suitable for that. Then treat him with the rest of treatment until he recovers.
The Thirty-Fifth Chapter.
For the removal of the toad-born under the tongue.
It may occur under the tongue a tumour resembling a small toad which prevents the tongue from performing its natural action and perhaps hardens until it fills the mouth; the treatment is for the attendant to open his mouth towards the sun and gaze at the swelling.
If he sees it as a swollen red or black mass with no sensation, do not expose yourself to it; it is cancer. If it is leaning towards the whiteness and has moisture in it, put an iron into it, cut him open with a smooth lancet and clear him from all sides.
If blood overpowers you at the time of your treatment, put powdered zaja on him until the bleeding stops, then return to your treatment until you remove it completely, then compress with vinegar and salt.
Then treat him with the rest of the suitable treatment until he recovers.
The Thirty-Sixth Chapter.
For the treatment of swelling of the tonsils.
And whatever growth occurs in the throat among other tumours may expose within the throat glands resembling those that occur outside, called tonsils if treated with what I mentioned in the classification and did not recover.
Therefore, look! If the tumor is hard like a boil in color and touch is little, do not approach it with iron. And if it is red in color and its origin is thick, do not also approach it with iron, lest there be bleeding. Rather leave it until it ripens; it may either soften or burst from within itself.
And if it is white in color, rounded and its origin is thin, this is what should be cut. The procedure for it is that you look before proceeding whether the warm tumor has completely settled or only decreased a little.
So then, seat the patient facing the sun and his head in your lap; have him open his mouth and take a wooden stick between your hands and press his tongue down with it. This is its shape.
You make it from copper or from brass, thin like a razor. If you press the tongue with it and the tumor becomes clear to you and falls on it with your sight, take forceps and insert them into the stone and pull it out as much as possible without drawing any of the serous membranes with it.
Then you cut it with this instrument, similar to scissors but its two ends are curved and very sharp. You make it from Indian steel or Damascus iron.
If you cannot prepare this instrument then cut it with a razor like this, its image.
Sharp from one side and not sharp from the other. After you cut each stone, cut the other in the same type of cut as it is, then after cutting have the patient rinse with cold water or vinegar and water.
If there is bleeding in front of him, rinse with water that has been warmed up with pine scales or fir leaves or something similar to them until the bleeding stops. Then treat him until he recovers. And sometimes growths other than the two stones will appear in his throat, so cut them as I have mentioned in cutting the stones, alike.
A woman was treated for a growth that had sprouted inside her throat, hitting the commissure with little sensation, which almost obstructed the airway and prevented her from eating and drinking water.
She was on the verge of death if she had remained for a day or two, and the growth had branched out from it until branches came out through her nostrils. She hastened to use forceps, inserted one into one of them, then pulled and a suitable piece detached itself.
Then she cut it where it reached from the nostril, then did the same with what had protruded from the other nostril. She opened her mouth, pressed her tongue against it, then inserted the forceps into the growth itself and cut a part of it, without bleeding but a little.
Then the woman's throat was relieved and she hastened from then on to drink water, then eat food. And it would not be long before I cut into that growth repeatedly over a long period of time, and the growth would leave behind something in place of what is cut until I finished with it.
It was cut and the growth inside her throat was removed, and it ceased to grow. Then it receded and I did not know what Allah had done with it afterwards.
Chapter Thirty-Seven.
On cutting a growth in the throat.
Which is called a uvula if it had descended to the throat and become swollen, and was white and rectangular, then it is called a column. And if it was thick at the bottom and rounded, then it is called an uvula. If we treated as mentioned in the division, and the treatment did not heal.
And I saw the hot growth had subsided from her and was thin, so it should be cut. And if there was something conjoined and rounded, and it did not have length, and it was red or dark in color or black, or without sensation, then it should be avoided to cut.
There is a defect on the gum, so if you see it on the cheek which I have mentioned in its whiteness and length, situate the patient in the shade of the sun and compress his tongue with the instrument which I have described then insert the forceps into the socket.
And pull it downwards and cut it with one of the instruments which I have mentioned in cutting the tonsils, and it is necessary that you do not cut more from it than what increased the original matter without excess, for if you cut more from it you will cause harm to the voice and speech.
Then, after cutting it, use what I have described in cutting the tonsils and treat it until it heals. And if the patient is timid about cutting it, then you should make a ruse for him without fear or concern and the way of making a ruse for him is to put his head in your palm.
Then compress his tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned, then take from the hot water which I have described in the chapter of numbing and knead it with a ball that is not cold, making it neither thick nor thin, and fill this mould with it, like this:
Its end where you put the medicine is like a spoon mould, and place the instrument with the medicine on itself and the patient lies on his side so that saliva flows out from inside his throat lest anything descends into it and harms him.

And enter the rod with the thread into a tube from above until the thread sticks to the gum, do this several times until you reach the desired amount of numbing of the socket then leave it alone, for it will soften and shed after three or four days. And if you need to apply the medicine again, redo it.
After the application, rub around the boil with a swab dipped in fat and absorb what surrounds it from the medicine. Then suck on cold water and treat from outside with poultices and from inside with emollients until it clears up. This type of treatment is safer than cutting and farther from fear.
And the abscess can also be treated with something gentler than cauterization and cutting. It is treated with decoction on this nature, one takes fungi, calumba, colocynth, gallnut, thyme, papyrus, and similar herbs, then they are all or some of them put together in a container and immersed in vinegar.
And it boils and the container is caulked with the mortar of wisdom, and in the middle of the lid there is a hole into which is fitted this apparatus cooled to this nature made from bronze or copper.
The end containing the resin is inserted into the mouth of the abscess until the steam rises into the abscess through the tube until it suffices the abscess, then it is repeated over it several times until it softens. And beware that this treatment is not made in the first occurrence of the boil.
For it often increases in the boil, and it should be done when its hot boil subsides. And if this apparatus is not available then take a reed rod and attach to its end an eggshell covering so that the mouth of the abscess does not burn.
Because the eggshell covers prevent the heat of the steam from burning the mouth, and this is one of the good treatments with safety.
The thirty-eighth chapter.

And the ailing person knows better where the nascent thing is and pushes it down or pulls his hand with the instrument up, all of that to the extent that he prepares himself until it comes out.
The thirty-ninth chapter.

Chapter Forty-four.
In which to make a cut in the abscess and open it.
The abscesses are of various kinds, each differing in its own treatment and incision, according to the type of tumour it is and what moisture it contains.
And the second kind is according to the places in which it occurs on the body, because the abscess that occurs on the head is not like the one that occurs on the buttocks, and the one that occurs in a place of fat is not like the one that occurs at a joint, each has its own law.
And among the abscesses, there are some that should not be cut until the pus in them is ripe and complete, and there are others which should be cut even though they are fresh and have not ripened fully, such as those close to joints.
Because the abscess, if it occurs close to a joint and its matter becomes old enough to putrefy what is around it may corrupt the ligaments or nerve of that joint and be the cause of gangrene of that member or the abscess is next to the chief part.
Because if you delay its cutting until it is ripe, you will have harmed the chief part of the body or it was close to the buttocks so you cut it fresh and not completely ripe which is near the buttocks lest the pus become putrid and discharge into the rectum and it becomes a festering sore.
And it is necessary to know the time of cutting abscesses which have fully ripened, and this is when the pain has ceased, fever has left, redness and pulse have decreased, and the tip of the abscess and all its signs are threatened.
And it is necessary to cut the abscess in the lowest part of its place, if possible, so that the pus may flow downwards more easily or into a thinner and more prominent part of the abscess. And let the cut be made longitudinally along the body, if the abscesses are in the hands and feet.
Places of muscles and tendons and nerves and sinews, in general in all flat places without bend to them. And if the place bends then he goes with bandage according as that place. And if the swelling is in fleshy places it is better to leave its bandage.
Until its inflammation subsides as we said completely, you should not apply a bandage to it before that, for the discharge from it would be much and very dirty and foul-smelling. And possibly his lips might become hard and cracked, and some of the tumors might break on the surface of the body when necessary or according to what the member needs.
It is necessary to use a single bandage for small tumors, and a wide bandage or many slits according to the size of the tumor for large ones. And some of the tumors should be scraped and cut if they have become like rags.
It had become in a certain case like it was dead, as with many purulent and suppurating swellings. And some of them split into a three-sided slit, and some were cut out like the shape of an artichoke leaf.
And some of them were treated with a circular slit and crescent-shaped slits, etc. from the incisions. And what did not have a head like smooth flat tumors should be bandaged with a simple bandage only. And if the tumor was large and had accumulated for a long time and was bandaged, one should not hasten to take it off so that all the discharge comes out at that time.
But he would take some of it out then return the swelling for another day and then take out some of the discharge as well, doing that gradually until all of it is taken out.
And especially if the patient is weak in power or a pregnant woman or a small child or an old man, for the vital spirit often dissolves with the discharge suddenly and perhaps the patient dies and you will not feel it. Be very careful about this matter, extremely cautious.
After you have pounded the swellings, you should cleanse the wound and examine it. If the wound of the swelling is small or if there is only one simple slit, then use the lint from cotton or flax. But if the swelling is large and there are many slits in the skin.
You should then insert a thread into every slit, until they meet each other. And if the swelling has had some of its skin cut off or scraped away, you should stuff it with dry cotton flax and bind it on for three days.
Then you should remove it and treat it with the ointments as is necessary until it heals. And if bleeding appears during your procedure, use cold water and vinegar after having soaked a flax cloth in them and applying it to the site of the bleeding several times.
If the bleeding continues, you should apply treatment and remedy and procedures which we have mentioned in many places of this book and its sections. And if it is winter time and the site of the swelling has a lot of nerves, you should wrap it with wine and hot oil.
And you should place it on the site. And if it is summer time and the sites are bloody, you should carry the dressing soaked with water and oil or wine and oil, all of that cold until, as we said, on the third day, the swelling should break open and be cleaned.
And you should use in its treatment what we have described until it heals. This is all the knowledge needed to treat swellings in general, and as for the detailed method of each swelling, we have explained how to treat it briefly and clearly.
The forty-first chapter.
For the cut on swellings which are exposed in the skin of the head.
There are small swellings exposed on the skin of the head, they are of the type of abscesses which have sacks inside resembling the pouches of a hen, and their types are many. Some of them are fatty and some contain moisture similar to pus.
And among them is what contains moisture resembling a broth and the like. And among them is what is hardened, solid and all of them are without danger in cutting and removing them unless you encounter a vein when cutting into them.
And the procedure for cutting into it is that you probe it first with a tool resembling this one called the madess, until you know what it contains. If what it contains is moisture, then cut into it with a cut along its length, and a simple cut on this shape:.
Begin the cut from line ~b~ to line ~j~, and if the moisture is released, then incise the sac which contained that moisture and cut it all out completely, leaving not a thing at all. For often it returns if something remains.
Then dip a thread into the greasy ointment, if it is available, or in salt water. Fill with it the wound and leave it for another day, for it will eat away what remains of the sac. Then redo on it the thread with the ointment a second time, and a third time as needed.
Until you are certain that nothing remains of the sac. Then treat the wound with ointments until it heals. And if the swelling contains fatty matter, then cut into it along this shape:.
Cut into it folded and the scissors in both sides of the wound and incise it from all directions, and exert your effort in removing the peritoneum which contains it. And if a vein interferes with you, do what I have described to you afterwards. And also do likewise in the swelling if it is hardened as a result of the cut.
And the treatment for it is as I have mentioned, and cutting into a hardened swelling is easier because of its little blood and moisture. And some of these swellings in the head of some people may not contain moisture at all, that being how I cut into a swelling in.
The head of an old woman, on which I found the tumour as hard as a rough stone; its colour was white and it could not be crushed even with a hammer, and if one were to throw at it with strength, there would be no effect. And this is not like other happening tumours in the head, such as those appearing on the heads of boys.
And when the opening of the ear is involved, make all its apertures simple incisions; then place a thin pad inside to facilitate the entry of the medication downwards, and treat it with what agrees with it from treatment.
The Second Chapter Forty-second.
In the incision on pigs that are exposed in the neck, these tumours are often exposed in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin and they can be found throughout the body; and what is exposed in the neck may sometimes be one, while at other times it may be many, and some of them can arise from others.
And every pig of this type will be found to have a specific sac inside it, just as the humps and tumours of the head that we described; and there are many types of these pigs, some of them frozen, some of them containing fluids, and some of them malignant and unresponsive to treatment.
And I have not seen one of them in good condition on examination, whose appearance was close to the color of the skin and which moved in all directions and was not connected to the nerve of the neck or artery or vein, nor was it swollen. It should be incised with a simple incision from top to bottom of the body in this shape from line ~g~ to line ~b~.
And it should be scraped all over and the edges of the skin should be sutured with a needle or two needles or many needles if necessary, as we have said in the case of tumours on the head; and it should be removed little by little and leave no vein or nerve cut off; but the instrument cutting should not be very sharp.
If your hand is not steady, do not make cuts, lest you cut what does not need cutting. If you cut a vein or an artery and become faint, put in the wound some powdered alum or some saffron to stop the bleeding.
Close the wound and leave it until the swelling subsides and the wound calms down, when the bleeding ceases then return to your work until you are finished. Then feel with your index finger if there is any remaining and take small pieces of pig's skin to cut them up and clean them.
If there is a large vein in the pig's skin, it should not be cut from its root but rather tied with a thin and tight thread and left until it falls out by itself without causing harm. Then stuff the wound with cotton cloth that has been dipped in the Egyptian ointment and treat it.
And if you cut all the pig's skin, it is necessary to bring together the edges of the wound and sew them up from its side after knowing that no suture has remained. If you see that a suture remains because the pig's skin was large.
It is necessary to direct the cut towards its root and belly and use suturing and what we have mentioned. And if there were pig skins with moisture in them, enclose them with a thin cloth where their place of ripeness appears to you and let the cloth be below as we said.
Then use after the cloth the poultice made with Egyptian ointment and similar ones to eat what remains of decay, until you see that the wound has become clean then treat it with herbal ointments for flesh until it heals.
The Third Forty-Second Chapter.
Regarding the incision of the larynx due to a tumour that occurs inside the pharynx.
The ancients have mentioned this incision in the larynx, and I have not seen anyone in our country who has done it. But as for those with asthma, they should avoid cutting into the larynx because it will be of no benefit to them.
In order that all the thoracic cavities and lungs become healthy, and as for those who have a hot tumor in the mouth or throat or tonsils, if there is no disease in the trachea, then it is necessary to use the incision of the larynx to escape from the damage which will be from suffocation.
And it is necessary, if we want this, that we cut the larynx under three circles of the trachea's circles or four small incisions in width between two circles as much as the incision is in the peritoneum not in the pleura and this place agrees with the incision.
Because it is fleshless and its blood vessels are far from it, if the doctor is cowardly, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat with a forceps then cut the skin until, if he reached the trachea, he should avoid the blood vessels if he saw anything.
Then he cuts the peritoneum which we have described, and he takes hold of the incision in the trachea from the sputum that comes out of it with what is crushed and from the interruption of sound, and he leaves the wound open for a time until the time passes in which there was fear of suffocation. If this time has passed, he sews the edges of the wound together with skin.
And he writes it down alone without pleura, then the remedies are used which cause flesh to grow until it heals. He said, the compiler of this book, the interpretation of this saying which we have written is that if they see the obstruction has blocked his throat one of these tumors they mentioned.
And the obstruction was near death and they intended for him to suffocate, so they went to cut the larynx in order that the obstruction breathe on the place of the wound some breathing and be saved from death. And it is commanded to leave the wound open until the disease has been resolved and its boundaries have become three days or so.
Then they were ordered to sew the wound and treat it until it healed. I myself have seen a maid take a sharp knife and send it down her throat where it cut part of the trachea, so I was summoned to treat her and found that she was as badly off as one who has been slaughtered, so I exposed the wound.
I found that the blood coming from the wound was slight, so I became certain that neither an artery nor a vein had been cut and the breath came out of the wound. So I sewed up the wound and treated it until it healed, and nothing but a faint coughing noise remained in the maid.
And she returned to her normal condition after a few days, so from this we say that cutting the trachea is not a hazard.
The Fourth and Forty-first Chapter.
Concerning the cut on the tumor which is exposed in the throat from outside and is called epiglottic fissure.
This tumor which is called the epiglottis can be a great swelling on the body's complexion and it is very common in women, and there are two kinds of it.
Either it is natural and there is no cure for it, or it is acquired and it comes in two kinds. One kind is similar to fatty tumors, and the other kind is similar to a swelling which results from an entanglement of an artery and in cutting it there is danger. One should not touch it with iron at all unless the part is small and she searches for it carefully with a probe and finds that it resembles fatty tumors and is not connected to any of the blood vessels, so cut it as one would on fat. And if it is in a sac, take out the contents and then treat the place with what is needed for treatment; otherwise, search out all of it and then treat the place.
The 44th Chapter.
In the cutting of various materials.
The materials are many in kind and have been mentioned all of them in the classification; and it is necessary that we mention here the difference between the material and the abscess, for indeed the abscess has heat, fever, and terrifying pains until the bleeding subsides. And the abscess becomes fetid; then the fever and inflammation subside. The material, however, does not have with it heat or fever or pains, but rather a sac which is its special container, similar in color to the body, which begins like an ulcer and turns into a swelling, larger or smaller.
It is of two kinds: either fatty, or it contains moisture, and the colors of the moisture are many as was mentioned in the classification. Therefore, if you come to treat the material, you must first probe it and search for it with the instrument called al-madass, as described in the chapter that precedes this one.
Measure the size of the tumor, then remove the madass and look at what comes out in its place. If a watery fluid of any color comes out, cut it with a simple incision, as I mentioned regarding other tumors. And if no fluid comes out when you remove the madass, know that it is fatty.
Cut it with a surgical incision in this shape as I have instructed you, and hang it on the scalpel's hangers; gently scrape the skin from all sides and preserve it in a sac if possible so that you can remove it together with the material in its correct form.
If the sac bursts during the operation and you are unable to remove it in its correct form, that often happens; then break it up into pieces until nothing remains of it. For if any part of it remains, either little or much, the material is accustomed to return to its usual condition.
If the swelling remains and only a little of it subsides, then when you are free from your other work, use some sharp instruments to clean out the wound thoroughly. Bind the wound tightly, then cover it with something that will cool the swelling. Treat it with the usual remedies until it heals completely. If the boil is large, make an incision in its corner and treat it as you would any festering wound.
If blood from an artery or a vein spurts out and there is the danger of haemorrhage, then first apply powdered alum to the affected area and leave it tied up for two or three days until the wound has ceased bleeding and the heat has subsided. Then return to cutting away any remaining part of the abscess.

Chapter Forty-Nine.
In the incision of the tumor which is exposed by the artery or vein and it is called aneurisma.

Chapter Fifty.
The Abscess which Erupts from a Nerve Twisting.
As the abscess erupts in the vein and artery, so also does the abscess erupt in the nerve if a blow occurred in it or excessive fatigue occurs or something like that, and it is more common in the places of the elbows and wrists.
And in every place where the joints move, there is a suppurating abscess which resembles the color of the rest of the body and it is usually painless, but if pressed with great force he feels a numbness similar to paralysis and the abscess is not collected in depth of the body.
If it is under the skin and moves in all directions, neither advancing nor retreating; what was of it in a joint should not be exposed with iron, for it may cause inflammation; what was of it on the head or forehead.
Cut the skin with a probe, if the swelling is small, then take hold of it with tweezers and cut it from its base; if it is large, burn it with a cauterizer and remove it; then close the wound by sewing and treat him until he recovers.
Chapter Fifty-One.
In cutting abscesses that are exposed in the abdomen.
Many abscesses are exposed in people's bellies and elsewhere on their bodies, which are called ulcers due to their resemblance to a fungus. In origin it is thin and its head is thick, its edges have turned over and some of them become very large.
And I have seen a man with two abscesses in his belly, they resembled things like fungi, no difference, white and thin at the base, their edges had turned over and were ulcerated, and moisture was constantly dripping from them. I cut them open and threw one on a scale and it weighed around eighteen drachmas and the other around six drachmas.
And the treatment for cutting them is to look, if the abscess is moist and the colour of the ulcer is a white wet thin base, then cut it open with a broad probe. And let the cauterizer be near the fire, because often much blood flows out when cutting them.
Then apply some leaded thread to it, if the blood gushes out. If you see the abscess is sluggish and trembles from the iron cut, take a strong lead thread and tie it tightly around the ulcer, let it be for two days then tighten the lead thread again so that it remains tied.
Whenever you intervene in an abscess until it dries up and falls from its place without any trouble, then if the abscess has a thick base, there is some fear and uncertainty about it, especially when it is in the abdomen. But sometimes half or part of it can be cut.
Then you must compress it so that it does not return, then treat it until the wound heals. And be cautious about cutting an abscess which is cold in color, little in sensation, and has a bad appearance; for it is a sign of cancer and we will mention cancer after this.
Chapter 52.
In the treatment of carbuncles.
A carbuncle occurs from many causes, either from a rupture of the peritoneum on the abdomen through which pus or an abscess comes out as in other ulcers, or from blood that flows from an artery or vein as mentioned before, or from a boil that forms under the skin.
If it is from a rupture of the peritoneum and outflow of pus, then the color of the boil will be like the color of the body, it will be smooth and without pain and its position will be different. And if it is from an outflow of pus, then its position will be with what we described as more different, and if you press it with your fingers, it will disappear and come back again, and perhaps there will be a crack in it and it will grow greatly when entering the bath or after great fatigue. And if it was because of moisture, then it will be smooth.
It does not disappear if you press it with your hand, nor does it grow or diminish. And if it is from blood, then in addition to these signs the boil will appear to be black. And if it is from a growth of fat, then the boil will be soft and spongy and will hold together like one piece.
And if it is from a boil, then its touch will be smooth. The treatment for that is to observe; if the carbuncle is from arterial or venous blood or a boil, you should abstain from treating it because there is fear and uncertainty as I have informed you in the chapter where I mentioned the ulcers that occur due to the arteries and veins.
If the wound of the abscess is from before the anus or the vulva, it is necessary that the surgeon order himself to stand up straight and then learn with a sponge around the entire abscess. Then order him to lie down in front of you on his back, then seize with a broad forceps around the abscess at the place where you learned with the sponge, then reach into the center of the swelling up high with a large needle and bind the place of the clamping with strong thread or cotton binding tightly.
And the knot of the binding is to be loose, then open the tightened swelling above the binding and insert your index finger and look for the anus. If you found it, that the binding has taken hold of it, loosen the knots and push the intestine into the abdominal cavity, and if you find a bowel, extend it with a stringed needle.
And cut its residue, and if a vein or artery opposes you, then seize it with forceps and return to your work, take two needles and insert strong threads into them, and enter the two needles into the clamping which you made around the swelling, parallel to it, then pull the swelling in four places on the needles.
And if you want to remove the needles and leave the place until the tightened flesh becomes putrid and falls off by itself or is cut out when it is rotten, then treat him with what is necessary of ointments until he heals, if the wound of the abscess was from a gangrenous flesh.
Or if it is due to moisture, then you must compress the swelling as we said and withdraw the blood or moisture that you find in it, then treat him with what heals the place.
The Third Chapter Fifty-three.
In treating cancer.
We have mentioned in the classification types of cancer and how to treat it with medicines and the warning from treating it with iron so that it may ulcerate, and we have mentioned the uterine cancer born and the warning from its treatment.
The ancients have stated that when the cancer is in a place where it can be removed entirely, like the one which is in the breast or in the thigh and similar movable parts, to remove it completely; especially if it is small. But when it has progressed and become large, it should not be approached.
If I was able to cure anyone from it, and I did not see any other that had reached that point before me, the procedure for this is, as we said earlier, to advance and then to break up the concretion in its veins, clearly.
Then the concretion is sutured in its place so that it may heal. Then instruments are inserted into the cancer which fit it, and it is wrapped around with skin on all sides, making sure nothing remains of its original root. The blood should be allowed to flow freely without being cut off quickly.
But compress the place tightly and let out all of the thick blood with your hand or whatever instruments you have. If it resists in the procedure, a great amount of bleeding will occur from cutting an artery or vein, so stop the flow until it stops, then treat him with the rest of the treatment until he recovers.

Chapter 57.
For the purifying of boys and for treating what can befall them as errors.
The circumcision is nothing but a disruption of connection like other incisions, except that since it is done by us of our own will and especially used on boys, then it is necessary for us to do the best in it.
And the easiest and safest method, I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books because it was not used among them, but rather is what we have acquired.
By experience and this is how the majority of craftsmen and barber-surgeons have found to use purifying with a reed and a razor, using threads and bandages and cutting with knives. And I have tried all these forms.
So I did not find better than purifying with a razor and bandaging with thread because purifying with a reed often results in the skin tearing, since the gauze has two layers, so perhaps the upper layer of the skin is cut but the lower one remains.
It is forced to be cut again and suffering renewed pain, and purifying with a knife does not guarantee that the tip of the penis will not be cut because it might enter its groove, and as for purifying with scissors then perhaps the skin slipped and spoiled your work or the boy's skin was short by nature.
Often they are born that way and do not need purifying, and I have seen that, and as for purifying with a razor and bandaging with thread the experience has shown me its superiority because the cut is uniform so that the blade from above is like the blade from below.
When you have straightened your hand to fit the two blades so that it cuts at a single measurement and in a single time then the thread becomes almost like a wall for the skin of the penis from all sides without any error, and the first intention of this work is that it should be comfortable for the boy.
But especially if the one who understands a little knows that you bind the thread in his hernia only, and leave it until another day then loosen and straighten him with every face, and he will be satisfied with that as much as his mind can grasp, then stop him before you standing upright.
And he should not be sitting and hide the scissors in your cloth or under your foot, nor should the child's eye fall on it at all, nor on anything of the instruments, then you put your hand into his hernia and blow up the skin until it comes out the head of the hernia.
Then you clean it from whatever dirt accumulates in it, then bind the area that is shown with a thread of two turns, then bind below it slightly a second suture, then grasp with your thumb and ring finger the place of the lower suture firmly and cut between them. Then lift the skin up quickly and bring out the head of the hernia, then let the blood run a little because that is better and less swelling of the hernia, then moisten it with a damp cloth, then sprinkle on it some dry roasted embers of olive tree wood, this is best among what I have tried or finely powdered charcoal, this is also excellent.
Then lift the skin up quickly and bring out the head of the hernia, then let the blood run a little because that is better and less swelling of the hernia, then moisten it with a damp cloth, then sprinkle on it some dry roasted embers of olive tree wood, this is best among what I have tried or finely powdered charcoal, this is also excellent. Then carry the embers on top of it in a cloth soaked like a hard-boiled egg in rosewater mixed with powdered rose water, and leave it until another day then treat him with the usual treatment until he recovers.
And this is an image of the scissors which are suitable for cleansing:.
They will be sharp and straight blades, without a notch for the pin, and the length of the blades will be as long as the handles, whichever. The 48th Chapter.
In the treatment of retained urine in the bladder.
The retained urine in the bladder is due to its blockage by a stone, or solid blood, or mucus, or growing flesh and similar things. If you treated that with what we have mentioned, types of treatment described in the classification.
And if the urine has not been released and you see that its blockage is by a stone which has become lodged in the neck of the bladder, then the operator should sit on his knees, then a man rides on his back and stretches his belly towards his back and holds the operator himself as much as he can.
At that time, the neck of the bladder is forced to push the stone behind and the urine will flow. And if it does not flow as mentioned and the condition becomes severe on the operator, then it should be extracted by a tool called catheter which has this shape:.
It is made from silver and is thin, smooth, and pliable like a reed tube. It is long, about a finger's width, and has a small funnel at its head. The way to draw out the urine with it is to take a bent thread and tie a soft wool or cotton string tightly at one end.
One inserts the end of the thread into the lower part of the catheter and wraps it with a cloth so that if something from the silk slips in to fill the tube, he stops it like a stopper. Then he dips the catheter in oil or fat or egg white and sits the operator on a chair.
He loosens his bladder and urethra with wet adhesives or oil and warm water, then he inserts the catheter gently until it reaches the root of the penis then he bends the penis upwards towards the navel then he pushes the catheter inside.
Until if the penis is bent then he pushes the catheter inside until it reaches close to the scrotum he leans the man downwards and the catheter inside then he pushes him until it reaches the bladder and the operator feels that it has reached something empty.
And this is made because the passage through which the urine flows is crooked, then he pulls the thread with silk with some force so that the urine follows the silk, then he takes it out and pours off the urine, and repeats the catheter.
He continues to do that until the bladder is empty and the operator finds it light.
The Fifty-Ninth Chapter.
How to drain the bladder with a bladder stone.
The instruments suitable for that are made from brass or polished ivory with a long tube on a flat base, and it is desired to pour water and medicines into it and this is called the stone-squeezer and this is its picture:.
It is made from polished brass or ivory with a long tube on an inclined base, all of it polished except for the end which is closed and there are three holes in it, two from one side and one from the other as you see.
The hollow place in which the two calipers are placed will be as full as it can possibly hold, without more of it being added, until a liquid is drawn out with it; and when something is pushed out with it, it will push out after him, just like the pitcher that is thrown into the sea.
If you wish to remove the moisture from the bladder, you will introduce the tip of the catheter into the moisture and draw with the caliper up; then the moisture will be drawn into the hollow of the catheter. Then you will insert its tip into the urethra as we have described in the catheters, and then push out the moisture with the caliper.
For that moisture reaches to the bladder in its place until it is felt by the patient, and here is also another soft catheter which they use to irrigate the bladder.
It is made from copper or spadra; its upper part resembles the small funnel and at the bottom there is a pocket where the ligature falls in, then take the bladder of a camel and put into it the moisture which you want to irrigate with into the bladder and then tie them together tightly with a doubled thread.
You will heat that moisture a little on the fire, then put the tip of the catheter into the urethra and pull your hand tightly onto the bladder with the moisture tightly so that the patient feels that that moisture has reached the bladder.

Then tie it to the device and do with it as you did with the bladder by holding your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter Sixty.
In the removal of stones (kidney or bladder).
We have mentioned in the classification the types of stones and their treatments with drugs, and the differences between those formed in the kidneys and those formed in the bladder, and the signs indicating that, and the stone on which an operation is performed by hand and cutting.
And it is the stone produced in the bladder especially which occurs in the urethra, and I am describing that clearly and briefly.
I say that the stone produced in the bladder is most commonly seen in children, and one of its signs is that the urine comes out of the bladder like water in clarity.
And it appears in him with sand, and its edge is scratched and played with, and often it hangs and spreads, and the perineum becomes prominent in many of them. And it is easy to remove stones from boys until they reach fourteen years old, and it becomes difficult for the elderly, but young men are intermediate in that.
And that whose stone is the greatest, its treatment will be easier, and the smaller one will be contrary to that. So if we proceed to the treatment, it is necessary first that the patient be injected with a syringe which removes all the sediment in his bladder, so that the existence of the stone may be prevented at the inspection.
Then the patient is taken and held upright, with his hands under his thighs, so that his bladder is tilted downwards, then he is inspected.
And he is examined from the outside, if you feel the stone in place then proceed to cut into it immediately. If it does not fall out, then take a finger, either the left thumb for children or the middle finger, and grease it with oil from the left hand.
If it is a complete boy then enter the catheter into his bladder and search for stones until one falls under your finger, transfer it little by little to the neck of the bladder, then press on it with your finger and push it out towards the place you want to cut.
And order a servant to compress the bladder with his hand and another servant to stretch the skin on either side towards above and beyond the place where the incision will be, then take the curved forceps whose shape is:.
And cut between the perineum and the scrotum, not in the middle but alongside the left iliac prominence, so that the incision is on the same side as the stone and your finger is inside the bladder compressing it to come out enlarged from outside and narrow from within as much as the stone can exit through it.
Not always, perhaps you squeezed the stone with your finger in the bladder at the incision so it comes out without difficulty, and know that some stones have corners and facets making it hard for them to come out.
And some of them are smooth like a plum and rounded so it comes out easily, but what has corners and facets you should increase the incision a little; if she doesn't come out like this it is necessary that you grasp her firmly with a sharp forceps whose tip is like a file.
So that it is stuck to the stone so it does not slip from it, or else you insert into under it a gentle instrument with a rounded end; if you can't do it then slightly increase the incision; if something of blood overpowers you cut it off with a cauter.
If there are more than one, then push the big one first into the bladder and cut it, then push the small one afterwards; do likewise if there are two or more of them; if they are very large, know that it is ignorant to make a deep incision in them because it exposes you to one of two dangers.
If he dies or if a constant dripping of urine occurs so that the area does not adhere at all, but try to push it until it comes out or turns in breaking with calabashes until it comes out certainly.
If you have finished your work, wash the wound with a binder and two sponges and tie it tightly, then pour on top of it an infusion of oil or drink or red ointment mixed with cold water to calm the hot swelling. Then let the patient lie on his back without loosening the bandage until the third day.
If it has dissolved, remove the area with a lot of water and oil then treat him with the olive ointment and the papyrus ointment until he heals. If there is an excessive hot swelling in the wound and like this, that blood congeals in the bladder and urine refuses to come out and this is known from the coming out of blood with the urine.
Then insert your finger into the wound and take out that blood because if it remains, it will invite corruption of the bladder and its stones. Then wash the wound with vinegar and water and salt and apply every kind of treatment which was applied to him until he heals.
It is necessary during all the times of treatment that his thighs be bound together and tied up to hold fast the remedies which are put on the place. If the stone was small and had become in the urethra and had stuck there and urine refused to come out, treat it with what I have described before it becomes in the cut.
Often have I dispensed with this operation and treatment by using this remedy which is to take a red-hot iron of the iron forge, its form being:.
A triangular tip sharp pointed like a spike at the end, then take a string and tie it around the urethra below the stone so that it does not go back into the bladder, then insert the red-hot iron of the spike into the urethra gently until the spike reaches the same stone.
Place the catheter in your hand, alongside the stone, a little at a time, as you seek to pierce it until it is perforated from the other side. For the urine will flow out of its channel then grasp with your hand what remains of the stone outside the catheter for it will shatter and come out with the urine and the ulcer will heal.
If you are hindered from this treatment by an obstacle, tie a thread under the stone and another above it, then cut through the stone in the catheter between the two threads, and it will come out.
Then the suture will close and clean out the stagnant blood that has accumulated in the wound. This suture was necessary so that the stone would not return to the bladder, while the other one from above so that if the first thread broke after the stone came out, the skin would return to its place and cover the wound.
And for this reason, you should lift the skin upwards when you tie the upper thread so that it will return to its place and cover the wound, as we said.
The 61st Chapter.
For Removing the Stone from Women.
A stone rarely develops in women. But if you find one, its treatment is difficult and often refused for many reasons, among them that the woman may be a virgin and another that you will not find a woman who will allow herself to be treated by a doctor.
If she is chaste or from the women of the mahrams, thirdly you will not find a woman who is skilled in this art and especially in operating by hand, fourthly that the place for cutting on the stone in women is far from the place where the stone is located so you need to make a deep cut.
And there is danger in that, so if necessity calls for it you should take a skilled female doctor and little do we find them, but if not available then seek a chaste and companionable doctor or prepare a skilled midwife in the affairs of women or a woman who can give some indication in this art.
Prepare it and order her to make everything that she orders her to examine, first the inspection of the stone. That is, look if the woman is a virgin, then insert the finger into her vagina and inspect the stone. If you find it and press it under your finger.
Then order her to cut it, if she was not a virgin and was married then order the midwife to insert her finger into the vagina of the woman and inspect the stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and compressing it well.
If you find it, then insert it from the opening of the bladder down to as much of its capacity as possible until it reaches the base of the thigh, then cut into her at the juncture of half the vagina at the base of the thigh from any side that the stone presents itself and she feels it in that region.
And her finger does not leave the stone compressed under it. Let the cut be small at first then insert the rod into that small cut. If she feels the stone, increase the cut to the extent she learns that the stone comes out from there, and know that kinds of stones are many.
Among them are small and large, smooth and hairy, long and twisted and having a beard. So know their kinds so you can guide yourself to what you want. If blood overwhelms you, leave it in the place of powdered and moistened clay and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops then return to your work.
Until the stone comes out, and work that you count with yourself among the tools I mentioned for removing the stone from men to assist you in your work. If bleeding overwhelms you and you knew by the pulse of the blood that it is from a severed artery, place the styptic on the place.
And bind it with compresses firmly and leave it, do not repeat and leave the stone and do not remove it. For perhaps the woman will have died, then treat the wound. If the bleeding has stopped after a few days and the place has softened, return to your work until the stone comes out.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
In the incision on the urinary bladder.
The urinary bladder is a collection of fluid in the white peritoneum which is under the skin of the scrotum surrounding the testicle and it is called the sacrum and it may have a special membrane for it that Nature has prepared on the side of the testicle.
Until it is thought to be another ovary and it will be between the skin of the testicle and the white peritoneum which we mentioned, but this would only happen in rare cases, and this bladder originates from weakness that exposes females so matter is assigned to it and it may become exposed due to a blow on the females.
And this moisture is of many colors, it may be yellowish in color or blood red or bloody dark red or watery white and that is more often the case, and its signs are known by.
Where the water gathers, it is then in the white peritoneum which we mentioned, so the swelling will be slightly elongated to the length like a shape of an egg and the testicle does not show up because the moisture surrounds it from all sides.
And if the moisture is in a sac for it, then the swelling will be elongated on the side of the testicle.
And for this reason a man will be mistaken that it is another ovary, and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicle and the white peritoneum then it can be felt, but if you want to know the color of the moisture, scrape the swelling with a square compress which we showed its picture beforehand, what comes out in the result judge according to that.
So if we resort to treatment with iron, it is necessary that the surgeon orders bleeding if possible and you see his body full then he lies on his back on something slightly raised and you put a cloth over him many times then sit beside him.
Order a servant to sit on his right side, extend his penis towards one of my sides of the scrotum and towards the direction of observation of the belly. Then take a broad lancet and cut the skin of the scrotum from the middle lengthwise to close to the anus.
The incision becomes on the straightness parallel to the line that divides the skin of the scrotum into two halves until it reaches the white serous membrane. You peel it off and beware that you do not cut it. The peeling from your side is more adherent to the testicle, and you take as much of the peeling as possible.
Then you press the full serous membrane with a wide flat spatula and drain all the water from it. Then you spread between the edges of the incision with pointed instruments and lift up the serous membrane without touching the skin of the scrotum that contains it, and cut the serous membrane as much as possible in one piece or in pieces.
Especially the delicate part, because if you do not take it all out, the water may return. If the testicle protruded outside its skin while you were working on it, once you have finished cutting the serous membrane, spread it and then join the edges of the scrotum skin with stitching.
Then treat it with the treatment of all incisions until it heals. If you have wounded the testicle, it may have become gangrenous from another disease, so tie the vessels in the scrotum to prevent bleeding, then cut the spermatic cord from the scrotum and take out the testicle and then treat it as we mentioned.
If the water collected on both sides is equal, know that they are equal in volume. Cut the other side as you have done with the first one, whether or not you intended to make the operation one-sided. Then clean up the blood.
You enter the incisions with a woolen thread that you have dipped in oil or rose oil, and it comes out from outside a woolen thread that you have dipped in wine and oil. You spread it on the testicles and belly skin, then put over them a folded cloth called "al-rafid" (the lining). It is tied from above with the strap which has six extremities like this:.
Then two straps are taken and sewn, stuffed with wool as shown in the example, and the extremities which are tied with them made of linen or wet wool, and gathered together by tightening in a belt for trousers. And one of the extremities is attached to the backrest to the spine.
And the second is taken to about the groin, and both ends are on the thighs from below, and the remaining two ends are on the armpits. And all the tightening is gathered in a belt for trousers. And this support can also be made with leather instead of being split with iron.
And it is that you take a gentle, thin needle file and split the scrotal skin as we described until the white membrane containing water is exposed. Then take another needle on this pattern:.
And it resembles the Greek eye, then you tie it with that membrane until all the moisture comes out. Then you stretch the membrane with forceps and scrape with a needle file the layer containing it, cut it as much as you can until you remove all of it, and preserve it from the egg so that the fire does not touch it.
Know that this work is more secure and safer than letting blood, and better than the operation with a cut. If a hot tumor or bleeding or something else interferes with you in the incision or when sewing, it should be treated as soon as possible with the treatment suitable for it as mentioned earlier.
If the disease is sluggish and has not tolerated this operation because of its severity, then the poultice should be used as I have described it. And if it is suitable for you according to what we have mentioned from the indications.
That the support is watery, so the patient should sit on a high chair then tie the tumor below with a wide sponge, and put the poultice along the length of the body and keep the opening wide so that all the water flows out, then place cotton on the place and tie it.
He dries him with the rest of the water, then treats him until the wound heals. If the water drips out when you press on it, it is only because the white membrane obstructs the exit of the water in the mouth of the wound and prevents its exit.
So then it is necessary to insert a feather of a goose or the instrument used for drawing out the water from boils, which has been depicted above or to slightly enlarge the wound.
Know that water may return and gather after six months or so. If it does, wrap him on the same condition and the doctor will defend his days.
Chapter 63.
In incision of the bloody abscess and its treatment.
Know that the incision of this abscess is from the wounds leading to death in most cases, so we see leaving it and being safe from it. And I remember treating it and its types of tumors.

If the flesh vegetation is in a place of adhesion which is from behind, it is fitting that you cut all of it and take out the egg as we said. If you have completed your work, fill the wound with damp wool soaked in rosewater and wine then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
The Fifty-Fourth Chapter.

The daliah is a twisted tumor resembling a cluster, with relaxation of the abdominal walls and difficulty in movement, exercise, walking; in the treatment of this affliction, similar to what has been mentioned previously.

And have a servant of yours hold it and extend it with great tension, then cut with a wide-bladed sharp scalpel an incision which follows the shape of the vessels until the vessels are revealed, then strip from all sides as I mentioned to you in the matter of cutting the veins in the groin, then insert into it a needle with a split thread.

Chapter Fifty-five.
In the treatment of intestinal worms.
This worm occurs when an opening is made in the peritoneum on the belly, about a span and a half from the navel, and the intestine comes out of this hole into one of the groin openings.
And this opening is either from a tear in the peritoneum, or from its extension; and these two types occur due to many causes: a blow, a jolt, a cough, lifting something heavy and similar things. And its sign, if it is from the extension of the peritoneum, that it gradually occurs over time.
And it does not occur suddenly, and the worm is evened out up to a certain depth before the peritoneum compresses the intestine. And its sign, if it is from a tear in the peritoneum, that it occurs at its beginning with an enormous pain all of a sudden, and the worm appears different under the skin nearby.
And that is by the intestine and its contents coming out, and going outside from the peritoneum. And it may come out with a piece of intestine in it, so this worm is called intestinal and intestinal-intestinal, and it may be accompanied by gas, and it may flow into the intestine and get stuck there, causing death to the patient.
Because it causes severe pain and cramps, especially if it is compressed. And the treatment of this condition with iron is dangerous and should be avoided, unless the patient returns the intestine to its place with his own hand when he wishes to do so.
Then he lies down on his back in front of you, raises his legs, and you stretch the skin below the navel upwards and cut all the skin of the scrotum by its length. Then you insert needles into the edges of the cut as much as needed to open it with them.
The incision will be of the size that allows the egg to come out, then strip away the serous membranes under the scrotal skin until the white firm peritoneum is exposed from all sides. Then insert your left thumb into what follows the egg.
Between the white peritoneum under the egg's skin and the second peritoneum, release the adhesion that is behind the egg. Then bend with your right hand towards the inside of the scrotal skin, while extending the white peritoneum upwards with your left hand and lifting the egg with it towards the incision.
Order the servant to lift the egg upwards and release completely the adhesion that is behind. Then inspect with your finger so that there is nothing from the twisted tube in the hard white peritoneum, if you come upon something push it towards the lower abdomen.
Then take a needle with a thick thread that has been twisted from ten threads and enter it at the end of the peritoneum under the scrotal skin next to the incision. Then cut off the ends of the needle's bend until there are four threads. Then twist some of it together in a spiral shape and tie with it the peritoneum which we said is under the scrotal skin tightly from two sides. Then also wrap around the ends of the threads and tie them tightly so that nothing from the vessels that feed it can reach it. So that a hot boil is not exposed from it and also another tie comes out of the first tie, far from it less than two fingers. And after these ties take from the peritoneum under the scrotal skin as much as the width of a finger.
So that a hot boil is not exposed from it and also another tie comes out of the first tie, far from it less than two fingers. And after these ties take from the peritoneum under the scrotal skin as much as the width of a finger. Cut off the rest all round and pull out with it the egg, then make an incision below the scrotal skin a bleeding cut as we described before, then use the wool soaked in oil and put it in the wound and use the tie which we described.
The white omentum which we mentioned after its removal is sewn up carefully lest there be bleeding, and the suture is left in place until it falls away of its own accord. If it does not fall off quickly, it is to be loosened by pouring hot water over it and then placing the patient in a position that causes it to drop off.
Then the wound is treated with the same treatment for wounds until it heals.

Chapter 71.
In an incision that occurs in the navel.
The incision in the navel may expose the place as we mentioned, and nothing from the intestines descends into the female parts, and if something did descend it was slight and returned to its place at all times.
But if time passes, the incision in the omentum increases and descends into the groin and exposes that from the extension of the omentum which is in the navel as we mentioned. For the omentum extends then stretches and pushes the place aside, and its treatment by cauterization as we have described.
And it is treated with iron on this condition, that the patient lies on his back between your legs, then cut the place of the incision which is warm and extends outward to a depth of three fingers, then sew up the membranes under the skin.
Until the white peritoneum is revealed, which lies above it. Then take a probe and place it on the spot arising from the peritoneum and push it to the depth of the abdomen. Then sew both ends of the peritoneum that appear at the end of the probe together with suture.

And silk is better in this place because it is closer to safety.
Chapter 67.
In relaxation of the scrotal skin.
Often the skin of the scrotum becomes relaxed in some people without the contents inside becoming relaxed, and it looks ugly. For one who wants to treat it, let him put a compress on his back.
He cuts all the skin that has relaxed on the thick skin. Then he gathers the edges, and if you wish to sew first a fold of the relaxed skin with three or four stitches and fasten the stitching, then cut what is between the stitches.
Then treat it with the treatment of all wounds until it heals and the sutures fall out.
Chapter 69.
In castration.
Castration in our religion is prohibited.
So I should not have mentioned it in this book of mine, but I have mentioned it for two reasons. One is so that the physician may know how to treat it if he is asked about it. The other reason is that we often need to castrate some animals for our benefit.
As mares, does and cats and similar animals from beasts, I say that castration is of two kinds either by pinching or by cutting and slashing. The one done by pinching in its operation that we sit the beast in hot water until the females become languid, relax and hang down.
Then you relax it with your hand until it comes loose and does not show upon being touched. And as for castration by cutting and slashing, one should hold the beast and compress the skin of its scrotum with the left hand then tie the testicles and cut a single incision on each one.
Until if the testicles appear, cut them after they have sloughed and do not leave on them anything except for the thin membrane that is over the vessels. And this kind of castration is better than the one done by pinching.
Because pinching may have left something of the female parts so that the beast becomes desirous of copulation. Then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
The treatment of a hermaphrodite.
The hermaphrodite in men is of two kinds, one that appears below the pubic area or on the skin of the scrotum between the female parts resembling a woman's vagina with hair and the urine can be seen dripping from what is in the scrotal skin.
And as for women, one kind which is above the pubic area on the vulva similar to the little boys' buts which extend outside, one resembling a man's penis and both resembling female parts, the treatment of the three kinds.
The two kinds of men and the one kind of women should have those excess tissues cut off until their mark disappears then treat them with the treatment of other wounds until they heal. And as for the second kind of men from whom urine comes out that is in the skin of the scrotum there is no operation on it nor any treatment at all.
The 71st Chapter.
On the amputations of the clitoris and the flesh which comes from the vaginas of women.
The clitoris may be larger than its natural size, so that it becomes ugly in appearance and sometimes very prominent in some women to the extent of becoming like men's genitals and thus being used for sexual intercourse.
You should grasp the clitoris with your hand or forceps and cut it off, without lingering in the cutting, especially not in the depth of the root so that bleeding is avoided.
Then treat the wound with a treatment for cuts until it heals, and as for the flesh that grows, it is meat that grows in the mouth of the uterus until it fills it.
And perhaps it will come out to the outside like an abscess. And so some of the ancients call it the abscess disease, so you should cut it as you would cut the clitoris and treat it until it heals.
The 72nd Chapter.
On the treatment of obstruction.
Obstruction is when the woman's vagina is not stitched or has a small opening and it can be either natural, born with it, or acquired, and if acquired then it may be from excessive flesh that has grown.
or a thin or thick membrane and it can be either in the depth of the uterus, or on its sides, or at the top or bottom and prevents intercourse, childbirth, and menstruation, and perhaps also prevents uterine contractions. And knowing this is by looking with a speculum.
If the obstruction is close and apparent, then if it is not apparent investigate with her fingers or a speculum. If the obstruction is from a thin membrane and is close to the vulva, hasten its rupture, which means placing on the vulva something like a sponge then place your fingertips of both hands together.
A woman lying on her back with her legs spread, then she should stretch the scissors with force until the thin peritoneum bursts and the suture opens. Then she takes wool and dips it in oil and puts it on the place and tightens the woman every day so that the place does not adhere again once.
If the peritoneum is thick and dense, it should be cut with a wide bistoury similar to an aspen leaf. If the suture is from fresh flesh, tie it with ligatures and cut it off. Let it be with you medicaments that stop bleeding without pain such as quinine and licorice mixed with egg whites.
Then use a wide lead tube so that the wound does not close quickly. Hold it for some days and then use flax oil, then treat with all the treatment of adhesion until it heals. And in case there is another flesh growth inside the womb, it should be cut off on this condition.
Unless it is a carcinomatous tumor, the carcinomatous tumor that is in the womb should not be touched with iron at all.
Chapter Seventy-Three.
In the treatment of hemorrhoids and anal fissures and red blisters that appear in the vaginas of women.
As for hemorrhoids, it is a swelling of the mouths of veins until much blood flows from them constantly. If the hemorrhoids are presented, they became anal fissures. And I have mentioned in the classification their kinds and signs and we will mention here.
What accepts treatment and what does not accept treatment, I say that hemorrhoids and anal fissures if they are deep in the uterus and do not show to the touch then there is no treatment with iron. And those that appear inside the mouth of the uterus which can be felt are the ones that can be treated.
It is necessary that the woman enter a cold house then she should insert the anal fissures with a file or a rough cloth and cut it from its roots then apply to it when bleeding from one of the arteries cutting off the blood without pain.
Like the cotton wool and the linen cloths and similar things. Then elevate her legs to the wall for a moment, then let them down in cold water. If the bleeding persists, put her in an aloes decoction with pine resin scales and mastich and similar things. Then take wheat flour and mix it with honey and vinegar.
And apply it to her back. If the bleeding stops, else enclose with a strong bandage and breasts without condition. Then take a poultice, immerse it in decoction of mastic or decoction of dates or decoction of Ulyuk's branches with mastich syrup, and compress the place.
If the swelling subsides, treat the place with ointment until it heals. But red vesicles resemble the heads of hares in rough appearance, so cut off what has appeared from them as I mentioned in cauterization, either way, and treat them until they heal.
Chapter Seventy-Four.
Concerning the abscess which appears in the uterus.

She brings her legs together towards the lower part of the belly and her thighs spread apart, and her arms are placed under her knees and bound with a bandage that fits.
So the candidate sits on the right, and uses the instrument with which she opens up the uterus to its appearance as shown later. The procedure hurts the patient. If the instrument is too deep, it is necessary to place a spatula on the neck of the uterus so as to prevent the entry of the entire instrument into the depth of the womb and it should be that the cord that runs in the instrument comes from the upper side.
And you are holding the instrument and the servant turns the cord until it opens the neck of the uterus. If a growth appears and is touched with the hand and is thin and liquid, then you cut it near its head with a wide lancet if all the flow has ceased.

It is necessary that she abstains from being treated with iron but is treated as mentioned in the section.
Chapter Seventy-five.
In the instruction of the cauterizer on how to treat living scurfs if they emerge in a manner other than their natural form.
It is necessary for the cauterizer to know first the natural form of childbirth. Among its signs, if the woman lets her body sag downwards and stretches that it breathe in the air and what appears from her as a result of delivery.
And the birth of the fetus becomes quicker. Know that this delivery will be in its natural form and the exit of the fetus is on its head with the placenta or suspended from its neck, so if you see these signs then you should press down her belly so that the fetus comes out quickly.
For if it comes out on its head the placenta will come down with it and it will be purified from those impurities in a good purification, and except for this delivery it is unnatural and condemned because the fetus may come out on its feet and its hands before its head and its feet.
And it may come out with one hand or one foot or its head and one hand or twisted and perhaps turned on its back and in such forms that are condemned, so it is necessary for the cauterizer to be prudent and gentle with all these things and beware of error and mistake.
And I am describing every form of it and how to proceed with it so that you can refer back to it, if the fetus comes out on its head which is the natural delivery and you press hard on the woman for that and it becomes difficult for her to give birth and I saw her strength had weakened, then sit her down on a chair and order women to tie her.
And cool her womb with the cooked fat and with wet palms, then the cauterizer enters between her fingers grasping a small instrument, she cuts or cuts it with her nails until what is inside of them in moisture comes out and presses down the woman's belly so that the fetus comes down.
If it does not come down, it is necessary for the woman to be given a drink of almond juice with anointing of the uterus then command her to strip and snuff with cotton wool and hold her mouth and nose because the fetus comes out of its amniotic sac. If the hands of the fetus have first come out, it is necessary to return them gently little by little.
If they do not come down to enter, place the woman on a bench and raise her legs up then shake the bench on the ground and the woman should hold something so she does not fall when shaken. If the hands have not entered and the fetus has died, take them out and pull out the rest of the fetus.
Or tie his hands with a cloth and pull them out gently. The fetus comes out on its feet, if the fetus comes out on its feet it is necessary to push them up then turn the fetus little by little until you straighten him then take one of his legs and extend it little by little.
If they come out to the thighs command her to strip and snuff with cotton wool then he comes out. If he does not come out as we described and otherwise, turn the fetus little by little until it becomes in its natural shape then he comes out smoothly. If it refuses everything like that.
Take from the spittle of the gullet and almond juice and anointing of the uterus and dissolved gum and mix them all in a mortar with good beating then pour it into the woman's vagina and lower back then sit her in warm water until the vessels.
If you see that it has softened below, make a poultice from dates and let her wear it. If you have held the poultice for an hour then sit her on the chair then snuff her and stop her mouth and nose and press her lower back with gentle pressure then the fetus comes out of its sac, the fetus comes out on its knees and hands.
If the woman has a stone or clots in her uterus, she should be laid on her back and her legs lowered to the ground while she is resting on her bed. Her hands are then brought up to her abdomen and squeezed lightly, lightly. Then, remove the pillows from under her legs until they are bent down. If the fetus does not come out, take both of her legs and move them strongly. Then, press above the navel lightly, lightly until the fetus rises up. The midwife then puts in her hand and gently feels the fetus.
And command the woman to undress until the fetus comes out. The fetus's head coming out crooked, bent towards one of her hands. Hold into pulling it back. If you are unable to pull it back, place the woman in a standing position and make her walk. If she is unable to walk, have her lie down.
Place the woman on her bed and shake her legs strongly, strongly. Then apply the crooked tool which I have described from the instruments.
