The fetus comes out on its mother's back, with its hands flat and its face towards the back of its mother. The midwife should hold the hand of the fetus then turn it gently, gently and straighten it softly. If it is straightened, carry it on its mother's back what we have described from ointments and instruments.
Then tell the woman to move a little, a little. If she does this, seat her on a stool and command her to lean to the right side. Then tell her to undress and blow into her with papyrus. Since it comes out, the fetus exits standing up on its side.
If it has descended into the womb with the afterbirth in this condition, split the afterbirth with your fingers until you free it from moisture. Then, if it is stuck to the face and neck of the fetus, cut them off from their origin lest it strangle and die. Then push the fetus back inside as needed.
Tell the woman to dry herself thoroughly and it will come out easily, like twins or multiple births. Know that twins are often born and three or four of them survive, though this is rare. As for five, it is something outside nature which do not survive at all.
And surround them and if they are many, an afterbirth for all of them, separate them with a membrane barrier between each one, tied in the womb. And sometimes they come out as the single fetus comes out naturally and easily, and sometimes they come out abominably, as we have described.
If some of them are stuck at birth and become as we have described, abnormal forms, then gently manipulate it as we have said. And let the woman be gentle and do what she does gently and carefully, and take care to prepare for any trick leading to safety.
Describe what is conceived in the womb of fetuses that fall, which sometimes conceive one and two and three and four and five and six and seven and more than ten. And it has been told to me that a woman miscarried seven and another fifteen all of them formed thus.
According to the wise, all-knowing estimate, this should be known by the woman, so that if it happens to her one day, she will meet it as needed.
Chapter Seventy-seven.
The removal of the dead fetus.
If the treatment for the dead fetus that I mentioned in the previous section is applied and it does not come out, and you are forced to take action by hand, then look at the woman. If she has good strength and there are no symptoms from which damage should be feared, then let the woman lie on a bed on her back.
Her head is tilted downwards and her legs are raised high. A servant adjusts it from both sides or ties it to the bed so that her body does not slide when the fetus is moved inside.
Then he moistens her cervix with wet compresses made from the juice of dates and spittle, and a piece of linen, as well as linseed oil. Then he dips his hands in these wet compresses and spittle, and inserts them gently into the uterus. Then he asks that it be placed in a position where the fetus's instruments can be inserted in its proper place.
Observe, for if the fetus is descending on its head, insert the instruments into its eyes or into its neck or mouth or chin or under its beard or between its shoulders or beneath the arms.
And if it is descending on its feet, into the groin and midribs. It should be grasped with the right hand and its tip should be turned between the fingers of the left hand and then inserted gently and insert an instrument into some of those places which we have mentioned.
Until it reaches an empty space, then another or third instrument is inserted into the opposite side so that the traction becomes even and does not lean to one side. Then it extends with a steady thrust, neither straight nor only forward, but moves in all directions.
So that it may come out easily, just as one does with a tooth when extracting it. And in between this is done, the thrust should be relaxed. If something becomes stuck to one side, then some of the fingers should be dipped in oil and inserted from that side to turn with it. And if some of the fetus comes out, the instruments should be moved to another place.
She should raise it slightly to do this until the fetus comes out completely. And if she pulls out a hand before the others and cannot pull it back because of its tightness, then a cloth should be wrapped around it and pulled on until all of them come out, and then cut off.
If in the joint of the hand or in the elbow, and thus you must do in the other hand and in the legs, if the head of the foetus is large and pressure is applied to its exit, or there is water gathered on its head, then you should insert a probing forceps between the fingers.
And with it, you should probe the head and let out the water or push it back with the instrument called the extractor which is shown in the picture following this.
Also, do this if the foetus has a large head by nature. Then probe the skull or crush it with the extractor as we said, and take out the bones with forceps. If the head comes out and pressure is applied at the elbow, then probe until the moisture in the chest becomes prominent.
If the chest then becomes compressed. If the chest does not become compressed and the exit is not achieved, cut in places as much as you can. If it is below the navel and warm or there is pus in it, then bind it until moisture seeps out from it.
If the foetus is on its legs then pulling it out is easy and placing it into the mouth of the uterus is simple. If pressure is applied to the belly or chest, then pull it out with a cloth that you have wrapped around your hand, and probe the belly or chest until what is inside them comes out.
If all the other organs have been removed and the head has been returned and stored, then let the midwife's left hand enter. If the mouth of the uterus is open, then insert the hand into the neck of the uterus, seek out the head with it, and pull it out with the fingers towards the mouth of the uterus. Then insert a hook or two hooks into it and pull it out with them.
If the mouth of the uterus has become compressed with a hot boil, then do not force upon it but rather when this happens use the pouring of moist and fat things. Use suppositories and sit in warm water that is wet and moist.
If the fetus is on its back, one should try to put it straight if possible. If that is not possible then it should be cut into pieces and delivered. The membranes should not be left inside at all. Once you have finished treating the case, apply the treatment for hot tumors which occur in the uterus.
If bleeding appears, lower yourself into a vise and apply the rest of the treatment. I have seen a woman who was pregnant, the fetus died inside her womb then she became pregnant again on it.
Then the other fetus also died and after a long time a tumor appeared in her belly, which swelled until it burst open and she was discharging its contents. I was called to treat her and I treated her for a long time but the wound did not heal. Then I placed some strong adhesive ointments on it.
Then a bone came out of the place and after some days another bone came out. I was amazed at this because the abdomen is not a place for bones to be. I suspected that it was from the bones of the dead fetus, so I explored the wound and extracted many bones from the head of the fetus.
I continued to follow that and extracted many bones from her, and the woman was in the best of conditions. And indeed she lived for a long time with a slight discharge coming out of that place. I have come here to record this rare case.
Because in it is knowledge and assistance for the physician who creates with his hand from treatment.

Chapter Seventy-eight.
In the delivery of the afterbirth.
If the afterbirth becomes stuck after delivery, then the midwife should grasp herself by the throat and blow into her mouth and nostrils; if it comes out with this method, otherwise take a quantity of air.
And pierce a hole in the cover, and put into it the open pith of the womb's mouth such as fumigation, and putrid tree resin, and chicory, and hawthorn, and banyan, and sassafras, and calumba, all these drugs or some of them, immerse in water and carry over a fire then place a silver tube on the hole in the cover and the other end into the womb's mouth.
And hold it until the steam reaches the bottom of the womb, then blow as we said; the afterbirth will come out quickly. If it remained after this treatment and did not come out, then order the midwife to dip her left hand in a fatty ointment or catarrh mucus.
Then she will insert it into the vagina and search with her hand for the afterbirth. If it meets it, then grasp it and pull it out slowly until it comes out. And if it is stuck deep in the womb, then insert the hand as we have described until you find the afterbirth, then pull it out little by little with caution.
So that the womb does not fall when pulled strongly, but it should be moved gently to the sides, right and left, then the pulling force is increased; at this time it will come out easily and be free from adhesion. And if the mouth of the womb was closed, we have described the treatment by blowing and with the container and pith.

It heals and comes out, unless it has been spoiled, in which case it smells bad going to the stomach and head. It hurts that place. One should use the appropriate poultice.
Therefore, some of the ancients tried a poultice made with cedar and unripe dates, the shape of the device that a woman uses when her menstruation is delayed and things like that.

The 77th chapter.
For the treatment of fistula in ano that has not been perforated.
Many boys are born with their anus not perforated and a thin fold of skin covers it, the patient should pierce that fold with her finger or else she will sew it tightly with a sharp needle and warn the muscle not to touch it.
Then she places a woolen cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then treats it with ointments until it heals. If she fears that it may close up, she should put a lead tube into the hole for several days and remove it when the child wants to defecate.
And the anus may also become obstructed due to an injury or a tumor, in which case one should cut through that obstruction and then treat it with what we have mentioned regarding treatment and lead.
The 80th chapter.
For the treatment of abscesses that occur in the lower part.
The abscesses that occur in the lower part are a complication and thickening that occurs near the anus from outside or in one of its cavities, and it is either one or more abscesses.
If you have cleared the coagulated substance from this complication, it will open and a white or turbid watery fluid may flow from it. Or it may be one of these nodes that has reached the rectum and the anus and is not drained. The draining one can be identified by what comes out of it in stool and flatulence when using the suppository to induce bowel movement.
And perhaps a worm will come out of it, and it may be one of these nodes if it is draining into the bladder and the urethra, or draining into the hip joint and the anal region. And what is known as a draining node to the rectum also from the non-draining one.
Put your index finger into the rectum, and insert a thin probe made of copper or iron into the node if it is not perforated. If it is perforated, then insert a soft lead probe or a hair from a horse's tail.
Until you feel with your finger the probe or the hair, if you do not feel it at all and nothing comes out of the wound in terms of stool, flatulence, or worm as we mentioned, then know that it is not draining. Therefore, hasten to the treatment.
And if the node is draining into the bladder or the urethra, then its sign is the urine coming out of it and it will not adhere to any medication. And as for if it is draining into the hip joint or the anal region, then its sign is reaching the probe there.
If there is no perforation to the bone and there is pain in that direction, and stool comes out of it always, and does not heal with treatment or adhere to ointment, then all these draining nodes are incurable.
And the treatment for it is trouble and falsehood to those who deceive with foolish doctors. And as for that which is not draining and not chronic, I hope for its cure with iron, as I have described it and experimented with it, which is that you place the suppository behind your back.
He should flex his leg upwards and bend it towards his abdomen. Then, insert a copper or lead probe into the navel until you learn where its end reaches. If the patient feels something being probed toward the seat of the pain in his back, you should put your index finger into the anus.
If you feel with your finger that the probe has been inserted openly without feeling anything between it and your finger or flesh, then know for certain that it is perforated. Do not tire in him, for he will not recover as we have said.
And they have said that he recovers in some people rarely. Until you learn that all those inflamed and swollen meats resembling a bird's feather tube have burnt, then treat him with an oily probe until they come out, then treat him with medicated ointments. If he recovers.
But if you inserted the probe and it did not reach your finger in the anus, while there was a thick veil of flesh or fat between them, and you saw the navel following the surface of the skin, then make an incision from the beginning of the navel. And you proceed with the incision along with the probe which is in the navel until the end of the probe reaches the point where it ended, and the probe comes out and falls. Then cleanse those inflamed meats resembling a bird's feather tube, leaving nothing behind.
Then treat him with medicated ointments until he recovers. But if the bleeding is heavy and hinders you from doing your job because of cutting those meats, do what will benefit you most quickly, either by cauterizing or a strong medicine, for cauterizing causes two good effects: burning the excess flesh.
Cutting the bleeding and purifying the humors, then treating it with greasy fat or crushed sulfur in oil until it infects the area, and that burned flesh comes out through the infection. Then treat the wound with embrocations made for hard flesh.
And these are the medicines in which aloe and purifying agents are mixed; if it coagulates, then he is cured and the ulcer will not recur. If the abscess has extended to the depth of the cavity and far from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the cavity and search with it.
If you feel the probe and between it and the abscess there is a veil of bone or flesh and it was near being absorbed, then there is no work to be done with it except by means of greed and hope. And that is that you use one of three methods, either that you crush it as we said.
Or else you cut into it until you reach its bottom so that you are able to insert the fat and treatment from close by, without lingering in cutting lest you cut through the surrounding muscle of the cavity and cause the anus to discharge excrement without intention. Then treat it as we mentioned, perhaps he will be cured as we said.
Or else you perforate that veil and clear it out after cutting into it close to the cavity as we said, either with a probe or another sharp edged tool. Then cleanse all those clotted bloods in the cut until you are able to reach them by probing.
Then pour the contents of the wound, together with the cut and upper mouth, until it is sealed. The abscess will remain open inside the cavity, and it will be less of a nuisance to the anus. And sometimes the abscess will dry up in this manner.
And if you inserted the probe into the abscess and it was in one side of the cavity towards the surface of the body with the skin and the ring of the anus, then take a punctured-pointed probe like the style of the scribe on this shape:
And insert into it a thread of five threads or thereabouts, then insert the suture needle with the thread into the nostril until its knot reaches, if it is inflated inside the recessed part from within nearby.
Then take out the thread from that hole by inserting your finger into the recessed part and taking out the end of the thread, then gathering both ends together, pulling them tight and leaving it for a day or two. Chapter Eighty-One.
In piles that bleed and are cut and the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Piles are of two kinds, either they are inside the rectum resembling bloody hemorrhoids or like the clusters of grapes and there are small and large ones and blood always flows from them.
And it is one and many, and it is outside the rectum and at its edges, but those that are outside the rectum are in most cases dry, yellowish liquid or little blood flows from them constantly and they are of the color of the body.
And the treatment of what is inside the rectum is that you order the patient to defecate and strain until the rectum comes out and the piles appear to you, then hurry and tie them with suture needles or hold them with your fingers and cut them at their roots, if they do not stick together due to their moisture and relaxation.
Clean it with a rough cloth or a piece of preserved ash, or bring it near your fingers; then cut it and sprinkle some sharp cauterizing substances on it so that they take the place of cautery, or do to her what has been mentioned in the chapter on cautery.
Then treat her with the rest of the treatment until she recovers. If the stool does not come out, inject the stool with a hypodermic needle containing a little hot water to cleanse it and hasten its exit when the impurity exits. Heal the exiting stools easily.
Take it with your fingernails or fasten it with forceps and cut it, then treat it as we mentioned until she recovers. And if one dislikes cutting with iron, one should use her thread in this way: take a loosened thread and insert it into a needle.
Then pull the abscess up and push it out with a needle in its root from the other side, twist the ends of the thread below the needle while it is bent back, and bind the abscess tightly; then tie the thread and remove the needle. Do this with all the stools, leaving one that you do not want to remove.
So that a bloody discharge can be drained from it, then put on the stool a cloth soaked in rose oil or cedarwood oil and place it on the stool; order the impurity to be calm and leave it until it falls. If the stools fall, treat them with ointments and all of the treatment until she recovers.
And as for the treatment of fissures, they often appear from the edges of the anal canal and arrest the natural temperament. If a remedy is applied to it and does not yield, then scrape it with a razor blade or your fingernails until it becomes soft and the top crust which prevents its union is removed.
Then treat it until it heals as is proper. If it does not heal, then re-cover it with a thicker dressing than the first one until it suppurates and breaks through, then treat it; it will recover.
Chapter Twenty-Eight.

It is necessary to cut around the splinter and grasp it with a pair of pincers or tweezers and pull out from its root then treat it, and if desired purify it as mentioned in its chapter. And as for the dry ulcers, one of them is a small rough, hardened, rounded spot on the surface of the body.
And it often occurs on the hands of boys. Its treatment is to stretch out the boil and cut it or cauterize it with a silk thread or a hair until it falls off, and if desired purify it with what has been mentioned before with fire or with the strong remedy.
And the inverted and non-inverted ulcers also come out with the instrument that I have mentioned in the treatment of scabies. And as for scabies, it is also a small, thick, moist spot on the surface of the body going deep into the flesh, and if it catches cold one feels inside it similar to the sting of an ant.
And it is in the whole body, and most of it is in the hands. Its treatment is to take a tube made from strong goose or eagle feather and insert that tube into the scabies until a circle of the tube surrounds it on all sides, then turn your hand with the tube until what is around the scabies is cut.

The Fourth and Eightieth Chapter.
In the treatment of wounds.
I have mentioned in the classification a treatment for burns and I am reminded here to treat them with the hand and drugs completely, so I say that wounds differ according to what the wound is made of and according to where the wound falls.
And the things that wounds are made of are many such as a rock bruise or sword cuts or knife cuts or an arrow wound or stick or spear and similar to these many things.
And as for wounds according to the places of the body such as a wound on the head or neck or chest or belly or liver and similar to these organs.
And I describe the treatment of some incisions so that they may serve as a measure and a law for all incisions. And I begin with the simple head injuries, especially because the complicated ones will be mentioned in the third chapter of this book.
And I say that if an injury occurs on the head, a simple wound not involving bone fracture, then if it is from a stone or similar substance and has only caused laceration of the skin, and the wound is large and there is fear of the formation of a hot abscess, proceed and cover with a poultice on the site. Do not delay in doing that, and remove from him blood as much as his strength allows, unless there is an obstacle to it, especially if the bleeding is easy, and let the bleeding be stopped from the opposite side of the wound.
And warn the patient to avoid fullness and drinking and thick food, if there is an obstacle to his bleeding then let him reduce his food and not approach meat or drink that are boiled. And apply on the wound a pad soaked in rose oil alone or with the drink in which camphor has been dissolved.
And if the abscess is prevented, then apply on the wound if it is moist with blood and the air has not changed its character which I will describe to you shortly. And as for if the air has changed its character, then apply some ointments on it.
Until the pus is drained then treat it until it heals. And if the wound is large and was caused by a cut of a sword or similar thing, and its edges did not meet with the flesh, then sew him up with stitches as I have described in stitching abdominal incisions.
And if the skin is exposed to bone and adhered and it was not united except for a small amount, then cut it off, then treat the wound with medicines that harden in it instead of skin. And order the patient to eat nutritious foods such as heads and trotters and similar things.
If there occurs a foul-smelling decay in the skin, and it has not adhered to the bone, cut away all of the decaying part and apply poultice to it. Then treat him, if in this wound there is a vein or an artery which bleeds blood from it and the bleeding has not been stopped with medicines, search for the vein.
If it has been pierced and it does not heal, scrape him with a curette and bind him. And if necessity demands, if what we have mentioned did not benefit, fill him up until the blood stops. If these wounds are small and simple, their treatment is easy, it suffices to sprinkle on them this powder while they are bleeding.
Before the air changes it, the powder is made by taking from the opium a part, from the alum two parts and from the well or unburnt gypsum three parts. Crush everything together and sift it, then fill the wound with it and tie it tightly until a good plaster adheres to it.
It is sealed with blood then tied from above with bandages and left, not being disturbed, as long as it does not swell. For if it swells, the treatment will be removed from him until he heals. And sometimes the gypsum alone can accomplish this, if the opium and alum are not available to you.
And sometimes this treatment can also be done with gum in many large wounds, if it is well placed and tightly tied on him, and the wounds are moist with blood and have not been changed by the air. But if they have undergone some change because of the passage of time, especially if it has occurred during summer.
In placing this powder, it means that he should be covered with some of the prepared poultices or a gruel made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until the pus dries, then treated with the rest of the treatment until he heals.
If the wound occurs and there is a fracture of bone that is slight, grasp it with the gauze. I have mentioned in what follows regarding the treatment of fractures of the skull, if the wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference in the treatment between this and a fracture of the head if it is slight.
And if there is a severing of the vertebrae or nerves, then if it is a vertebra, there is no remedy other than to avoid its treatment with a grip that is tight like a pincer and a forceps and the like because they harm the nerve and make it tremble.
And nothing cold is put on the wound at all because of the nature of the nerve being cold and its connection to the brain which is the most noble of organs, and any treatment he applies from liquid medicines such as moistened aloe with sweet water, or diluted oil, or rose and pomegranate ointment.
If it is also washed with sweet water and the rest of the metal stones on this feature and wet ointments, and as for if the wound is large, then apply suturing or compress his lips with a poultice then treat him until he recovers.
If there is a cavity in the wound and something has become lodged inside it that has accumulated mucus, then cleanse it in its lowest part. And if an artery has been severed in the wound and you catch his blood to be bleeding, then stop it or tie it up or cauterize him if necessity demands it.
And if the wound has cut some or all of the rings of the windpipe and you have loosened the ligatures, then bring together the edges of the skin with suturing on the rod of the windpipe without touching the windpipe but smear it and cover it as is its natural shape then tighten it tightly and leave him for a while.
Then treat him with ointments that have coagulation and drying until he recovers. And if the wound has affected the bone, then clean it out. And if there are fragments of bone in it, then take them all out or as much as you can take out, and do not leave any of it, unless you cannot, then let it be until the wound heals and dries up and it becomes easy to remove.
If the wound is moist, pour on it the dust that we have described. If it dries in the wound and a bone becomes prominent and suppurates, treat it with what will be mentioned under its heading in surgical procedures of the chest and between the shoulders.
If it was a stab with an arrow or spear and you saw pus in it, then look; if breath came out of it when the patient breathed out, know that it is a wound caused by fighting. If there was no pus and it was moist with blood, do not put dust in it from first to last lest the blood becomes stagnant in its depth.
He should be frightened in the heart and killed, but make a poultice on it attractively and apply it twice a day. If the poultice does not come to you, put cotton wool into the mouth of the wound so that it absorbs what comes out from moisture, and have the patient sleep on top of the wound.
Whatever accumulates in it will come out, and if three days or more have passed since the wound was inflicted and no bad movement or fluttering has occurred in the patient, nor any shortness of breath, and all his conditions are good, then know that the wound is safe; treat it with lint and continue the rest of the treatment until he recovers.
If it becomes difficult to see and the pus keeps flowing out constantly, know that a bone has become prominent; treat it from its page. The patient on the wound will have something come out of it. If three days or more have passed since the chest or back was wounded, treat it as mentioned before in sewing.
If it is large or has pus, if small, then if the bone was affected and pieces were cut from it, search the wound and hasten to remove those pieces if they are clean; but if they are not clean, leave them until.
If the wound dries up, it is easier to remove them; as for other wounds that occur in all parts of the body, their treatment should be judged according to what we have mentioned.
Chapter Eighty-Five.
Concerning the surgery of the abdomen and the removal and suturing of the intestines.
The wound which is exposed to the abdomen can be large, small or medium-sized; if it is large intestines may come out of it, or several intestines, and their insertion and suturing will be more difficult.
And also the small wound can be difficult from another point of view, so its closure is more difficult; and the intestines if they are not inserted in their place in time become swollen and thickened, making it hard to insert them. Therefore, the medium-sized wound is the best because returning the intestines does not cause difficulty with it, just as it causes difficulty in these two cases.
Know that the suturing of the abdomen is by four sides; two general suture types are suitable for suturing the abdomen and other surgical wounds, while the other two special types are exclusively used in the suturing of the abdomen.
And I will describe it to you one by one, explaining and clarifying; so I say that if the wound is small and something from the intestines has come out of it and its return is difficult, this is for one of two reasons: either because of the smallness of the wound as we said, or because the intestines have been inflated due to the cold air having entered.
So if it is like that, it should be warmed up by dipping a sponge or wet cloth in warm water alone, or having herbs such as chamomile and safflower and cardamom cooked in it, and then using this to massage the intestines until the inflation subsides.
And he may also do this by the drink which has been squeezed and is better than water alone in relieving the inflation; so if you see that the inflation has subsided, then insert the intestines with a drink of boiled bread or baker's yeast, for it will calm its entry with ease.
If returning to him after this treatment is difficult, then make a small incision with the tool that cuts knives and the first treatment if possible is better than cutting and it becomes necessary to cut only by force and inability of devices. And here is an image of the tool:.
Its direction is single and crooked, and the other direction is unlimited. And the thin end should not be sharp like the knife but rather a little thicker, it is a small instrument similar to that which you see. If the wound expands and the intestine enters, then its return should be on its natural shape.
And its place is specific, if you are able to do so, it is better. But if the incision is wide and in the lower abdomen, then the patient should lie on his back with his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper abdomen, he should make his head and chest higher than his lower body.
And likewise, if the incision is in one of the sides of the abdomen, then always make the side with the surgery higher than the other side. And it should be used thus in great operations and medium-sized operations.
And as for small operations, place him according to what you are able. Then prepare a close servant who grasps the incision with both hands and brings together its edges, then he uncovers it bit by bit for the seamstress.
And this is the characteristic of the common seamstress, that she takes a needle or several needles according to the width of the wound, then leaves from one end of the incision as thick as the thickness of the forceps and inserts a single needle without entering a thread into the edges of the skin. With the edges of the peritoneum which are inside under the skin from inside until it is perforated from that side. And I have gathered the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the peritoneum and they have become four layers, then she pulls with a doubled thread around the needle several times from both sides altogether until the wound edges meet in a firm gathering.
Then leave the thickness of the finger also and insert another needle, then entwine it with thread as I did with the first needle, so keep doing that until you need more needles to finish filling all the wound. Let the needles be in moderation between being thick and thin.
Because needles that are too fine cut into the flesh very quickly and it is difficult to insert them into the skin, therefore they should be moderate in thinness and thickness. And do not insert the needle near the edge of the skin.
So that the flesh does not tear quickly and the wound does not open up before it is stitched. And also do not stretch it too much with sewing, lest the wound refuses to heal. Then cut the ends of the needles so they do not hurt the patient at night and make him have abscesses from every side, tie the threads of the needles together.
And leave them until you know that the wound has healed, and this type of sewing with needles is most effective in small injuries because it can be sewn with one or two needles or something like that.
Or as for the quality of sewing in a second, common kind, it is that you sew the four edges together at once, meaning the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the membrane with one needle having thread of moderate thickness and coarseness, then if it is completed with this needle, pull the needle out from the side where it started.
So that the thread is entwined from above the wound, so that the sewing is like the sewing of a sack which holds things together, and make between each stitch after leaving the thickness of the small finger, and this type of sewing is known by everyone.
And with this type of sewing, I have stitched a wound that was shown to a man in his abdomen, he had been cut with a knife and the wound had become more than a finger breadth wide and had come out from his navel about two fingers worth towards the middle part of the belly, it was open in the middle of the abdomen.
He recovered after he had remained in a state of coma for twenty-four hours. The wound took about fifteen days to suppurate and I treated him until it was clean and he lived many years afterwards, behaving normally. The doctors used to say that he would never recover at all.
And it is remarkable that I did not treat him with an ointment because in the place where I was, there was nothing of the remedies. So I used to put on the wound cotton wool twice a day and promised to clean it with honey water until it healed.
And as for one of the kinds of suturing that is special to me, I remind you of a phrase from Galen's words: You start with the suturing from the skin and enter the needle from outside inward. If the needle has traversed the skin and the muscles running straight in all of the belly.
I left the edge of the peritoneum on the side where I inserted the needle and had the needle traverse its other edge from inside to outside in the other fold of the peritoneum. If it traversed, I then traversed it again in this same edge itself from the peritoneum outwardly.
And I left the edge of the peritoneum in this side and had the needle traverse its other edge from inside to outside. And as it traversed, it traversed with it into the fold of the peritoneum on his side until all of it was traversed.
Then I also began from this side with it and sewed the edge of the peritoneum in the other side along with the other edge of the peritoneum. And I extracted the needle from the skin that was beside it, then returned it to that skin and stitched the edge of the peritoneum in the other side along with this edge of the peritoneum itself.
And I extracted it from the skin that was beside it, and I did that again and again until all of the stitches were sewn in this way. And the whole description of this suturing is that it is a stitch like the weaver's threads for weaving.
The suturing of the omentum once from one side with the edge of the skin and leaving it free from the other side until emptying, And as for the second type of stitching specifically mentioned by Galen, this is his word.
And it is that you stitch them on the example of what some practitioners stitch, by gathering each part to its corresponding fellow which has problems, and they join the edge of the omentum to its other edge and the edge of the peritoneum to its other edge, this will be as I described to you.
It is necessary that the needle be inserted in the edge of the peritoneum close to you from the outside and it should perforate inside there alone, and leave both edges of the omentum then return the needle and perforate from the outside to the inside in both edges of the omentum then also return.
And perforate it from inside to outside in the edge of the other peritoneum which is on the opposite side, and this type of stitching is better than the general easy suturing which I mentioned, for that is Galen's word literally, and some say a stomach can be sutured with two needles. And that is to insert one thread into it and start by inserting the needle from you and perforate it to the other side, and insert the other needle from the opposite side so that it perforates from you as the stitching of sacra is.
Know that the rupture if it is in the middle of the belly, then its stitching is more difficult than any other place in the belly, and as for treating the wound, its judgment in its treatment is like the judgment of all wounds, so if you realized the wound fresh with blood before the air changed it and returned the contents and drew a line and strengthened it, then load on it the plastered lint.
If the wound has been exposed to air, then apply some ointments on it which are prepared so that they rot and the threads fall off and the intestines and the peritoneum become stuck together. Then treat it as you would any other wound until it heals.
If you do not have remedies, then apply on it cotton which has begun to rot and replace it twice in the day as I taught you until it heals. For most cases you will not need another treatment if the wounds are simple. But if you fear that the wound may involve the main organs in pain.
It is necessary to soak wool in lukewarm oil or rose ointment and place it around the areas between the armpits and chest. If he feels pain or bad smell in his boil, then treat him with a black tea infusion that is cool.
And especially if the foul odor has reached inside his boil and it has become an open wound inside him. Know that what was thick of the intestines is easier to heal, and what was thin of them is harder to heal.
As for the boil known as the abscess, it does not accept healing from any surgery on it at all because of its many and thick veins and its soft and fleshy substance and closeness to the nature of the nerve. And if what emerged from the wound was a filament and you caught it fresh, then take care of it just like you would the abscess itself either way.
If it has passed the time and it has turned green or black, then pull it with a thread above the place from which it became black so that blood does not ooze out. For there are veins and arteries in the filament, then cut what is below this ligature.
And make the ends of the thread to be tied from below the wound outward so that it is easy for you to pull and remove when the filament drops off and the wound rots. Mention the wound which appears in the abscess, if a small hole appears in the abscess.
A man had been stabbed with a spear in his abdomen on the right side of the stomach. The wound became inflamed and purulent, with diarrhea and flatulence emerging from it. I treated him by doing nothing more than what I shall describe. I did not touch him until he recovered and the place had healed. Then when I saw that the place had healed, I was afraid a worse accident would happen to him inside and it did not bring him any harm at all, but rather remained in his best condition. He eats and drinks, copulates and enters the bath, and remains in his service. Some people experienced have said that if he is shown to urinate with a wound and it was small, it should be sewn like this.
He is taken the big ants with large heads. Then, his wound's lips are gathered and an ant from them is placed open-mouthed on the lips of the wound. If it is pinched and its mouth clamped, then its head cuts off, then it adheres and does not come apart. Another ant is then placed near the first one.
And it continues to do this with many ants as much as the wound, then he turns him back and sews the wound. For those heads remain adhesive in the rectum until the intestines are healed and there is no harm whatsoever to the patient. And sometimes the intestine can also be stitched with a thin thread.
The thread that comes from the ant's sticky fluid after it enters a needle. That which is taken from one end of this thread, it drips honey, then it is tied with a thread of fine cotton yarn and then the thread is inserted into the needle. There is also a thread from the ant's fluid which he sews with the intestine then returns to the abdomen. And this type of sewing with ants and ants' fluid is only by chance and hope.
As for the case where there is a wide and large rupture, especially in one of the intestines, there is no remedy for it at all.
The eighty-second chapter.
In the treatment of phlegm and catarrh.
Know that every wound or tumor, if it ages and becomes a sore that does not heal and continually discharges pus, is called in general catarrh wherever the organ was located, and we call it phlegm.
It is a hard white abscess, true to its nature, without pain, and it has a cavity like the cavity of a bird's gall.
And for that reason, some people called it "riyah" (which means feather in Arabic), and sometimes it becomes moist and continually discharges pus, and the moisture may sometimes cease; and this moisture can be abundant or scarce, thick or thin.
And I have mentioned in the classification, when discussing wounds, that every sore which does not heal and in which meat does not grow is due to one of nine reasons; one of them being a scarcity of blood in the body; or its covering; or because there is solid flesh inside it and on its edges preventing good flesh from growing. And it may be because the pus and discharge are plentiful and foul; or that the sore itself is a corruption and the material discharging from it is of bad quality; or because the treatment does not agree in its cure; or because there was an ulceration in the region due to the disease; or because the place was peculiarly susceptible.
And it may be because the pus and discharge are plentiful and foul; or that the sore itself is a corruption and the material discharging from it is of bad quality; or because the treatment does not agree in its cure; or because there was an ulceration in the region due to the disease; or because the place was peculiarly susceptible. As I have mentioned in the city of Zaragoza, where healing illnesses is difficult and the discharge of tumors is slow by nature; or because there is a single bone or several bones in it. And I have pointed out all these causes and their signs and treatments with medicines in the classification.
It is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment of abscesses and flux that occurs by means of work with the hand. Know that abscesses occur in all members of the body, some leading to great sinews or vessels, others to nerves.
Or to sinew or to gut or to bladder or to rib of the ribs or to vertebral column or to joint of the compound joints compounded much like the hand and foot, some leading to near a principal member and similarly.
But if these abscesses are of this kind, they are among the difficult diseases that do not accept treatment and management, for they are troublesome and obscure. If however one of the abscesses has not reached these places which I have mentioned and hoped and wished to cure them.
And I wanted you to know this, take a probe made of copper or iron if the abscess runs straight and probe it with that, if there is convolution in the abscess, probe it with a probe of fine lead because lead softens its body.
It will become clear upon entry and turn towards the convolution, if the abscess has many openings that you cannot grasp with a probe then inject into one of its mouths at once, for the moisture which you inject into it will follow towards the other mouths and flow.
Then examine the place with probing again for any reason you can to know if there is bone or nerve or was the abscess's seat far or near, or that there are several abscesses with many openings, and be aware of all this with your ability to investigate, and note the pain when you touch with your finger on the place.
And similarly from the signs and reasons that occur to the tumor, so if you have been aware of all this in reality then at that time rely on the treatment with confidence, which is to observe, if it was.
The abscess is apparent, whether it is close to a joint or nerve or artery or vein, or one of the places I have mentioned to you. Cut the abscess in the way described and remove from it what is in it of matter and spoiled flesh and excess flesh.
And if there is growth in his mouth from flesh or ulcus and the like, treat him until he is healed. If the abscess is deep and straight, it is necessary that you cut it deeply as much as possible then cleanse it of all spoiled flesh.
Then use the spoiled lint in hot remedies and pour it into the bottom of the abscess which you will reach with iron, do that until he eats all the remaining spoil inside the abscess.
Then bind him with the ointments that cause flesh to grow correctly until he is healed. If he does not heal by this, then treat him as its description has been mentioned before. If the reason for the abscess is a bone and you know this, probe it and cut it in the way I have informed you if nothing prevents you.
A vessel or nerve or a main organ as we said. If the bone is revealed to you and it has some spoil and darkness, then scrape it until its spoil goes away then treat him in what makes flesh grow until he heals. If he does not heal and his putrid matter remains as it was.
Then understand that you have not reached the removal of all spoil, so uncover and scrape all what is on him again and thoroughly cleanse his scrapings with your best effort then bind him. If he heals, otherwise understand that this spoil is in a deep place from the spoil, so uncover and scrape all what is on him again.
And thoroughly scrape his scrapings and cleanse him with your best effort, if the spoiled bone is a small bone which you can remove it, so remove it with soft calabashes that are suitable for this.
If there are many bones, investigate their extraction thoroughly and do not leave anything undone. If something from the ligaments gets in your way without any danger of cutting them, cut those ligaments and the flesh if there is any and free the bones.
If you do not have enough time to extract the bones, carry on the wound whatever will putrefy it and leave it for some days until what is around those bones from flesh and ligaments putrefies and keep the wound so that the cut which you made in the middle of your work does not adhere.
But put on it if you feared that, a thread soaked in crushed sulfur with oil or a thread soaked in Egyptian ointment or one of the green ointments. Then, if those ligaments have putrefied and the bones are clean, extracting and pulling them will be easy.
If there is a big bone, such as the tibia or femur and the like, and only its surface has putrefied, remove it cleanly until that darkness and putrefaction goes away then close the wound. If the part that has putrefied is large and the putrefaction has reached into the bone, it must be spread out.
And cut it all the way to where the putrefaction ends, then close it until it heals. And I inform you of a gangrene that was presented to a man in his leg to make an example and guide for your treatment, and this man was young.
Tending towards thirty years old, gangrene presented itself to a man in his leg for a reason that moved inside the body until it connected with the leg and suppurated a large abscess and was not caused by something from outside then time passed together with the mistakes of the doctors until the abscess burst open.
Materials were drained from him in great quantity and his treatment was poor until the leg suppurated and many mouths appeared all of which vomited filth and bodily fluids, a group of doctors treated him for about two years without there being skilled by hand.
Until I approached, I saw his leg and the materials were flowing from those openings like a great stream, and the man's body had swollen and turned yellow. So I inserted the probe into one of those openings and the probe flowed to the bone, then I searched all the openings.
I found that some of them flowed into each other from all sides of the leg. So I probed and split one of those openings until I exposed some bone, and I found it to be rotten, hardened, blackened, putrefied, and perforated until the hole reached the brain. I spread out what was revealed to me.
I managed to remove the rotten bone, and I think there was no other corruption in the bone except what I had cut and spread out, and that I had extracted it. Then I made sure the wound would not heal for a longer time by using medications of strong remedies, but then I returned and uncovered the bone again above the first incision.
I found the corruption connected to the bone, so I spread out what appeared to me also from that corruption. Then I made him apply pressure again but it did not heal and then I uncovered it again. I did not stop cutting the bone a little by a little and urging his application of pressure until I cut about a span from the bone.
I removed it with the brain, and then I made him apply pressure using remedies and he healed quickly and was cured. This repetition in his treatment and suturing was due to the weakness of his limb and its inability to hold up, and my fear for his death because every time there was excessive bleeding which would cloud over and then clear completely.
And a hard, dense flesh grew in the place of the bone and his condition improved in his body and his strength returned and his movement became normal and he was not troubled with an affliction that would harm him at all, if it had been that a new bone had formed in a place in the body that had broken.
It is necessary to bind him with a bandage so that it reaches the end of the bone and order him to be raised upwards, and make another bandage from thick wool than the first.
Then tie him to the flesh beneath the bone and stretch its end so that the flesh is pulled downwards, and you expose the flesh from the place where you want to spread it lest the saw damage the flesh, and place a plank or board under the bone from below firmly.
Because if you do that, the saw will not be prevented from cutting the rotten bone, and it should be spread slightly above the place of the rot so that if there is rot inside the bone it does not show in its surface for feeling, and then you would have to spread it again.
If the bone is rotten and not disjointed but some of it is connected to each other with rot in its middle or some of it, then remove the flesh from all sides then place the plank from below and spread him from the first side where the rot is.
If you have finished spreading him, then spread him from the other side and let the spreading be a little away from the rot as we said, if the rot is in a joint cut off the rotten joint itself and spread the bone where it connects from the other side.
If the rot is in the connection of two joints, then there is no remedy but to amputate, if the rot is in a palm or foot strap, then the matter of its treatment is very difficult but you should peel off the rot whenever it becomes clear to you and clean it and dress it anyway you can.
And by what means will you be able to set it straight when the tendons or nerves get in your way, and know that the saws and knives for cutting these bones are many according to the position of the bones and their arrangement and thickening and roughness and size and fragility. Therefore one must prepare an instrument that suits each kind of operation.
Know that the operations themselves may inform you of the type of instrument you need, if you are familiar with the arts of this craft, for one skilled in this art and knowledgeable about its principles can observe many forms of disease.
